855

856 <section id="_1">

857

858 <h2>

859General Information About Plasma Cell Neoplasms</h2>

860

861 <div id="_section_1" class="pdq-sections">

862<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

863<h6>

864In This Section</h6>

865<ul>

866<li>

867<a href="#_4_toc">

868Incidence and Mortality</a>

869</li>

870<li>

871<a href="#_7_toc">

872Clinical Presentation and Evaluation<ul>

873<li>

874<a href="#_9_toc">

875Evaluation of patients with monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein)</a>

876</li>

877</ul>

878</a>

879</li>

880<li>

881<a href="#_16_toc">

882Monoclonal Gammopathy of Undetermined Significance (MGUS)</a>

883</li>

884<li>

885<a href="#_31_toc">

886Isolated Plasmacytoma of Bone</a>

887</li>

888<li>

889<a href="#_35_toc">

890Extramedullary Plasmacytoma</a>

891</li>

892<li>

893<a href="#_38_toc">

894Multiple Myeloma<ul>

895<li>

896<a href="#_40_toc">

897Prognosis</a>

898</li>

899</ul>

900</a>

901</li>

902<li>

903<a href="#_43_toc">

904Amyloidosis Associated With Plasma Cell Neoplasms </a>

905</li>

906<li>

907<a href="#_512_toc">

908POEMS Syndrome </a>

909</li>

910</ul>

911</nav>

912<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

913<a href="/types/myeloma/patient/myeloma-treatment-pdq">

914Go to Patient Version</a>

915</div>

916<p id="_3" tabindex="-1">

917There are several types of plasma cell neoplasms. These diseases are all associated with a monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein). They include monoclonal gammopathy of undetermined significance (MGUS), isolated plasmacytoma of the bone, extramedullary plasmacytoma, and multiple myeloma.</p>

918<p id="_312" tabindex="-1">

919For more information, see the <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/b-cell-lymphoma-treatment-pdq#_28">

920Lymphoplasmacytic Lymphoma (Waldenstr&#246;m Macroglobulinemia)</a>

921 section in B-Cell Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment.</p>

922<section id="_4">

923<h3 id="_4_toc">

924Incidence and Mortality</h3>

925<p id="_5" tabindex="-1">

926Estimated new cases and deaths from multiple myeloma in the United States in 2023:[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

9271</a>

928]</p>

929<div class="pdq-content-list">

930<ul id="_230">

931<li>

932New cases: 35,730.</li>

933<li>

934Deaths: 12,590.</li>

935</ul>

936</div>

937</section>

938<section id="_7">

939<h3 id="_7_toc">

940Clinical Presentation and Evaluation</h3>

941<table id="_8" class="table-default expandable-container">

942<caption>

943Table 1. Clinical Presentation of Plasma Cell Neoplasms</caption>

944<colgroup>

945<col width="25.00%">

946<col width="25.00%">

947<col width="25.00%">

948<col width="25.00%">

949</colgroup>

950<THead>

951<tr>

952<th align="Center" scope="col">

953Plasma Cell Neoplasm</th>

954<th align="Center" scope="col">

955M Protein Type</th>

956<th align="Center" scope="col">

957Pathology</th>

958<th align="Center" scope="col">

959Clinical Presentation</th>

960</tr>

961</THead>

962<TFoot class="pdq-footer">

963<tr>

964<td colspan="4">

965Ig = immunoglobulin; MGUS = monoclonal gammopathy of undetermined significance. </td>

966</tr>

967</TFoot>

968<tbody>

969<tr>

970<td>

971MGUS</td>

972<td>

973IgG kappa or lambda;

974

975or

976

977IgA kappa or lambda

978</td>

979<td>

980&lt;10% plasma cells in bone marrow</td>

981<td>

982Asymptomatic, with minimal evidence of disease (aside from the presence of an M protein) [<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

9832</a>

984]</td>

985</tr>

986<tr>

987<td>

988Isolated plasmacytoma of bone</td>

989<td>

990IgG kappa or lambda; or

991

992IgA kappa or gamma

993</td>

994<td>

995Solitary lesion of bone; &lt;10% plasma cells in marrow of uninvolved site</td>

996<td>

997Asymptomatic or symptomatic </td>

998</tr>

999<tr>

1000<td>

1001Extramedullary plasmacytoma</td>

1002<td>

1003IgG kappa or lambda;

1004

1005or

1006

1007IgA kappa or gamma</td>

1008<td>

1009Solitary lesion of soft tissue; most commonly occurs in the nasopharynx, tonsils, or paranasal sinuses [<a href="#cit/section_1.3">

10103</a>

1011]</td>

1012<td>

1013Asymptomatic or symptomatic</td>

1014</tr>

1015<tr>

1016<td>

1017Multiple myeloma</td>

1018<td>

1019IgG kappa or lambda; or IgA kappa or gamma</td>

1020<td>

1021Often, multiple lesions of bone</td>

1022<td>

1023Symptomatic</td>

1024</tr>

1025</tbody>

1026</table>

1027<section id="_9">

1028<h4 id="_9_toc">

1029Evaluation of patients with monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein)</h4>

1030<p id="_10" tabindex="-1">

1031Idiotypic myeloma cells can be found in the blood of myeloma patients in all

1032stages of the disease.[<a href="#cit/section_1.4">

10334</a>

1034,<a href="#cit/section_1.5">

10355</a>

1036] For this reason, when treatment is indicated,

1037systemic treatment must be considered for all patients with symptomatic

1038plasma cell neoplasms. Patients with MGUS or asymptomatic smoldering myeloma do not require

1039immediate treatment but must be followed carefully for signs of disease

1040progression.

1041</p>

1042<p id="_231" tabindex="-1">

1043The major challenge is

1044to separate the stable asymptomatic group of patients who do not require

1045treatment from patients with progressive, symptomatic myeloma who may need to be

1046treated immediately.[<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

10476</a>

1048-<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

10498</a>

1050]</p>

1051<p id="_11" tabindex="-1">

1052Patients with an M protein in the serum and/or urine are evaluated by some of the following criteria:

1053</p>

1054<div class="pdq-content-list">

1055<ul id="_232">

1056<li>

1057Measure and follow the serum M protein by serum electrophoresis or by specific immunoglobulin (Ig) assays; however, specific Ig quantification always overestimates the M protein because normal

1058Ig are included in the result. For this reason, the preference is often that baseline and

1059follow-up measurements of the M protein be done by the same method.[<a href="#cit/section_1.9">

10609</a>

1061]

1062Quantitative serum-free light chains (FLC) may be helpful to follow response when an M protein is not apparent.</li>

1063<li>

1064Measure and follow the amount of M protein light chains excreted in the

1065urine over 24 hours. Measure the total amount of protein excreted over 24

1066hours and multiply this value by the percentage of urine protein that is

1067M protein, as determined by electrophoresis of concentrated urine protein. An easier, but less accurate, method uses a spot-urine protein electrophoresis.</li>

1068<li>

1069Identify the heavy and light chain of the M protein by immunofixation electrophoresis.</li>

1070<li>

1071Measure the hemoglobin, leukocyte, platelet, and differential counts.</li>

1072<li>

1073Determine the percentage of marrow plasma cells. Be aware that marrow plasma-cell distribution may vary in different sites. Bone marrow is often sent for cytogenetics and fluorescence <em>

1074in situ</em>

1075 hybridization testing for genetic markers of high-risk disease. For more information, see the <a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_53">

1076Genetic factors and risk groups</a>

1077 section.</li>

1078<li>

1079Measure serum-free kappa and lambda light chains. This is especially useful in cases of oligosecretory plasma-cell dyscrasia or for following cases of light-chain amyloidosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.10">

108010</a>

1081] The FLC ratio of over 100 can predict a greater than 70% progression within 2 years in patients with smoldering myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_1.11">

108211</a>

1083] </li>

1084<li>

1085If clinically warranted, obtain needle aspirates of a solitary lytic bone lesion, extramedullary

1086tumor(s), or enlarged lymph node(s) to determine whether these are

1087plasmacytomas.</li>

1088<li>

1089Evaluate renal function with serum creatinine and a creatinine clearance.</li>

1090<li>

1091Electrophoresis of concentrated urine protein is very helpful in

1092differentiating glomerular lesions from tubular lesions. Glomerular lesions,

1093such as those resulting from glomerular deposits of amyloid or light-chain

1094deposition disease, result in the nonselective leakage of all serum proteins

1095into the urine; the electrophoresis pattern of this urine resembles the serum

1096pattern with a preponderance of albumin.<p id="_233" tabindex="-1">

1097In most myeloma patients, the glomeruli function normally allows only the small molecular weight proteins, such as light chains, to

1098filter into the urine. The concentration of protein in the tubules increases

1099as water is reabsorbed. This leads to precipitation of proteins and the

1100formation of tubular casts, which may injure the tubular cells. With tubular

1101lesions, the typical electrophoresis pattern shows a small albumin peak and a

1102larger light-chain peak in the globulin region; this tubular pattern is the

1103usual pattern found in myeloma patients.</p>

1104</li>

1105<li>

1106Measure serum levels of calcium, alkaline phosphatase, lactic

1107dehydrogenase, and, when indicated by clinical symptoms, cryoglobulins and

1108serum viscosity.</li>

1109<li>

1110Obtain radiographs of the skull, ribs, vertebrae, pelvis, shoulder girdle,

1111and long bones.

1112</li>

1113<li>

1114Obtain a spinal magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) scan (or spinal computed tomography [CT] or positron emission tomography [PET]&#8211;CT scan depending on availability) if the skeletal survey is negative.[<a href="#cit/section_1.12">

111512</a>

1116-<a href="#cit/section_1.14">

111714</a>

1118] At diagnosis, whole-body PET scan or MRI of the total spine and pelvis appears to be equally efficacious in the detection of bone lesions.[<a href="#cit/section_1.15">

111915</a>

1120,<a href="#cit/section_1.16">

112116</a>

1122]</li>

1123<li>

1124If amyloidosis is suspected, perform a needle aspiration of subcutaneous

1125abdominal fat and stain the bone marrow biopsy for amyloid as the easiest and

1126safest way to confirm the diagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.17">

112717</a>

1128]</li>

1129<li>

1130Measure serum albumin and beta-2-microglobulin as independent

1131prognostic factors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.18">

113218</a>

1133,<a href="#cit/section_1.19">

113419</a>

1135]</li>

1136<li>

1137The presence of circulating myeloma cells is considered a poor prognostic

1138factor.[<a href="#cit/section_1.20">

113920</a>

1140] Primary plasma cell leukemia has a particularly poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.21">

114121</a>

1142,<a href="#cit/section_1.22">

114322</a>

1144]</li>

1145</ul>

1146</div>

1147<p id="_14" tabindex="-1">

1148These initial studies are often compared with subsequent values at a later

1149time, when it is necessary to decide whether the disease is stable or

1150progressive, responding to treatment, or getting worse.</p>

1151<p id="_15" tabindex="-1">

1152The major challenge is

1153to determine which patients are stable, asymptomatic, and do not require

1154treatment, and which patients have progressive symptomatic myeloma who may need to be

1155treated immediately.[<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

11566</a>

1157-<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

11588</a>

1159,<a href="#cit/section_1.23">

116023</a>

1161]</p>

1162</section>

1163</section>

1164<section id="_16">

1165<h3 id="_16_toc">

1166Monoclonal Gammopathy of Undetermined Significance (MGUS)</h3>

1167<p id="_17" tabindex="-1">

1168Patients with MGUS have an M protein in the serum without findings of multiple

1169myeloma, macroglobulinemia, amyloidosis, or lymphoma and have fewer than 10%

1170 of plasma cells in the bone marrow.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

11712</a>

1172,<a href="#cit/section_1.24">

117324</a>

1174-<a href="#cit/section_1.26">

117526</a>

1176] Patients with smoldering myeloma have similar characteristics but may have more than 10% of plasma cells in the bone marrow. </p>

1177<p id="_18" tabindex="-1">

1178These types of patients are asymptomatic and do not need to be treated. Patients with MGUS and risk factors for disease progression, however, must be followed carefully because they are more likely to develop myeloma (most commonly), amyloidosis, lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma, or chronic lymphocytic leukemia and may

1179then require therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.26">

118026</a>

1181-<a href="#cit/section_1.28">

118228</a>

1183]</p>

1184<p id="_19" tabindex="-1">

1185Virtually all cases of multiple myeloma are preceded by a gradually rising level of MGUS.[<a href="#cit/section_1.29">

118629</a>

1187-<a href="#cit/section_1.31">

118831</a>

1189] The annual risk of progression of MGUS to a lymphoid or plasma cell malignancy ranges from 0.5% to 1.0% in population-based cohorts.[<a href="#cit/section_1.32">

119032</a>

1191,<a href="#cit/section_1.33">

119233</a>

1193] This risk ranges from 2% to more than 20% in higher-risk patients.</p>

1194<p id="_20" tabindex="-1">

1195Risk factors that predict disease progression include the following:</p>

1196<div class="pdq-content-list">

1197<ul id="_21">

1198<li>

1199An abnormal serum-FLC ratio.[<a href="#cit/section_1.32">

120032</a>

1201,<a href="#cit/section_1.34">

120234</a>

1203]</li>

1204<li>

1205Non-IgG class MGUS.</li>

1206<li>

1207A high level of serum M protein (&#8805;1.5 g/dL).[<a href="#cit/section_1.32">

120832</a>

1209,<a href="#cit/section_1.34">

121034</a>

1211]</li>

1212</ul>

1213</div>

1214<p id="_449" tabindex="-1">

1215 A Swedish cohort study confirmed that an abnormal serum FLC ratio and a high level of serum monoclonal protein are high-risk factors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.33">

121633</a>

1217] The study described the additional risk factor of immunoparesis, which is defined as the reciprocal depression of the other Ig classes (i.e., if a patient has an IgG kappa M protein, the IgM and IgA would be below normal levels with immunoparesis). Incorporation of gene-expression profiles to better assess risk is under clinical evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_1.35">

121835</a>

1219] </p>

1220<p id="_450" tabindex="-1">

1221Monoclonal gammopathies that cause organ damage, particularly to the kidney, heart, or peripheral nerves, require immediate therapy with the same strategies applied for the conventional plasma-cell dyscrasias.[<a href="#cit/section_1.36">

122236</a>

1223] A monoclonal gammopathy causing renal dysfunction&#8212;by direct antibody deposition or amyloidosis&#8212;is referred to as monoclonal gammopathy of renal significance.[<a href="#cit/section_1.37">

122437</a>

1225] Rising serum creatinine, dropping glomerular filtration rates, and increasing urinary&#8211;albumin excretion are all parameters that may signify renal damage and are assessed prospectively for high-risk MGUS patients. Although the N-terminal pro-brain natriuretic peptide is a very sensitive marker for amyloid involvement in the heart, the low specificity must be noted. These extra tests are included with the M-protein level, FLC levels, and FLC ratio when following patients with MGUS.[<a href="#cit/section_1.38">

122638</a>

1227] </p>

1228<p id="_663" tabindex="-1">

1229In a retrospective review of 6,399 patients with newly diagnosed multiple myeloma, 44 patients were found to have a biclonal IgG or IgA MGUS. The overall response rate of the myeloma clone to induction therapy was 93%, compared with 64% for the separate-clone MGUS (<em>

1230P</em>

1231 = .001).[<a href="#cit/section_1.39">

123239</a>

1233][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1234Level of evidence C3</a>

1235] Many MGUS plasma cell clones were unresponsive to available myeloma therapy; this result highlights the need to lower expectations for response in situations in which an MGUS may require therapy because of end-organ damage.</p>

1236</section>

1237<section id="_31">

1238<h3 id="_31_toc">

1239Isolated Plasmacytoma of Bone</h3>

1240<p id="_32" tabindex="-1">

1241The patient has an isolated plasmacytoma of the bone if the following are found:</p>

1242<div class="pdq-content-list">

1243<ul id="_33">

1244<li>

1245A solitary lytic lesion of plasma cells on skeletal survey in an

1246otherwise asymptomatic patient.</li>

1247<li>

1248A bone marrow examination from an uninvolved

1249site contains less than 10% plasma cells.[<a href="#cit/section_1.40">

125040</a>

1251-<a href="#cit/section_1.42">

125242</a>

1253] The absence of plasma cells on flow cytometry of the bone marrow suggests a low (&lt;10%) risk of recurrence after radiation therapy of the isolated bone plasmacytoma.[<a href="#cit/section_1.43">

125443</a>

1255]</li>

1256</ul>

1257</div>

1258<p id="_34" tabindex="-1">

1259MRI may reveal

1260unsuspected bony lesions that were undetected on standard radiographs. MRI scans of the

1261total spine and pelvis may identify other bony lesions.[<a href="#cit/section_1.44">

126244</a>

1263]</p>

1264</section>

1265<section id="_35">

1266<h3 id="_35_toc">

1267Extramedullary Plasmacytoma</h3>

1268<p id="_36" tabindex="-1">

1269A patient has extramedullary plasmacytoma if the following are found: </p>

1270<div class="pdq-content-list">

1271<ul id="_37">

1272<li>

1273Isolated plasma-cell tumors of soft tissues, most commonly

1274occurring in the tonsils, nasopharynx, or paranasal sinuses.</li>

1275<li>

1276Negative findings on skeletal x-rays and bone marrow biopsy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.45">

127745</a>

1278-<a href="#cit/section_1.47">

127947</a>

1280]</li>

1281</ul>

1282</div>

1283</section>

1284<section id="_38">

1285<h3 id="_38_toc">

1286Multiple Myeloma</h3>

1287<p id="_39" tabindex="-1">

1288Multiple myeloma is a systemic malignancy of plasma cells that typically involves multiple sites within the bone marrow and secretes all or part of a monoclonal antibody. </p>

1289<section id="_40">

1290<h4 id="_40_toc">

1291Prognosis</h4>

1292<p id="_42" tabindex="-1">

1293Multiple myeloma is highly treatable but rarely curable. The median

1294survival in the prechemotherapy era was about 7 months. After the introduction

1295of chemotherapy, prognosis improved significantly with a median survival of 24 to

129630 months and a 10-year survival rate of 3%. Even further improvements in prognosis have occurred because of the introduction of newer biological therapies and better salvage options, with median survivals now exceeding 10 years.[<a href="#cit/section_1.48">

129748</a>

1298] Patients with plasma cell leukemia or with soft tissue plasmacytomas (often with plasmablastic morphology) in association with multiple myeloma have poor outcomes.[<a href="#cit/section_1.21">

129921</a>

1300,<a href="#cit/section_1.49">

130149</a>

1302] Racial disparities because of socioeconomic factors, genetics, differences in risk factor exposure, and structural racism are under evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_1.50">

130350</a>

1304] </p>

1305<p id="_41" tabindex="-1">

1306Multiple myeloma is potentially curable when it presents as a

1307solitary plasmacytoma of bone or as an extramedullary plasmacytoma. For more information, see the sections on <a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_31">

1308Isolated Plasmacytoma of Bone</a>

1309 and <a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_35">

1310Extramedullary Plasmacytoma</a>

1311.</p>

1312</section>

1313</section>

1314<section id="_43">

1315<h3 id="_43_toc">

1316Amyloidosis Associated With Plasma Cell Neoplasms </h3>

1317<p id="_44" tabindex="-1">

1318Multiple myeloma and other plasma cell neoplasms may cause a condition called amyloidosis. Primary amyloidosis can result in severe organ dysfunction, especially in the kidney, heart, or peripheral nerves.[<a href="#cit/section_1.51">

131951</a>

1320] Clinical symptoms and signs include the following: </p>

1321<div class="pdq-content-list">

1322<ul id="_371">

1323<li>

1324Fatigue.</li>

1325<li>

1326Purpura.</li>

1327<li>

1328Enlarged tongue.</li>

1329<li>

1330Diarrhea.</li>

1331<li>

1332Edema.</li>

1333<li>

1334Lower-extremity paresthesia.</li>

1335</ul>

1336</div>

1337<p id="_511" tabindex="-1">

1338Accurate diagnosis of amyloidosis requires histological evidence of amyloid deposits and characterization of the amyloidogenic protein using immunoelectron microscopy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.52">

133952</a>

1340] In one series of 745 consecutive patients, 20% of patients with nonamyloid light chain amyloidosis (usually transthyretin) had an <em>

1341innocent</em>

1342 monoclonal gammopathy, indicating the significant risk of misdiagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.52">

134352</a>

1344]</p>

1345<p id="_372" tabindex="-1">

1346Elevated serum levels of cardiac troponins, amino-terminal fragment brain-type natriuretic peptide, and serum FLC are poor prognostic factors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.53">

134753</a>

1348,<a href="#cit/section_1.54">

134954</a>

1350] Proposed staging systems for primary systemic amyloidosis based on these serum levels require independent and prospective confirmation.[<a href="#cit/section_1.53">

135153</a>

1352,<a href="#cit/section_1.55">

135355</a>

1354]

1355 An increase in levels of serum FLC over many years can precede the clinical diagnosis of amyloid light chain amyloidosis.[<a href="#cit/section_1.56">

135656</a>

1357] Amyloidosis associated with an IgM monoclonal gammopathy is a rare, but distinct, clinical entity with more frequent neuropathy and adenopathy and less cardiac involvement.[<a href="#cit/section_1.57">

135857</a>

1359]</p>

1360</section>

1361<section id="_512">

1362<h3 id="_512_toc">

1363POEMS Syndrome </h3>

1364<p id="_513" tabindex="-1">

1365POEMS (polyneuropathy, organomegaly, endocrinopathy, monoclonal gammopathy, and skin changes) syndrome is a rare paraneoplastic condition associated with a plasma cell dyscrasia of early or late stage. The acronym describes a constellation of findings often marked by polyneuropathy, organomegaly (usually splenomegaly), endocrinopathy, monoclonal plasma cell dyscrasia, and skin changes.[<a href="#cit/section_1.58">

136658</a>

1367] Both sclerotic or lytic bone lesions and lymphadenopathy (with possible Castleman histology) may be identified. Anecdotal reports suggest remissions have been achieved using myeloma-directed therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.59">

136859</a>

1369-<a href="#cit/section_1.63">

137063</a>

1371] </p>

1372</section>

Am J Hematol 88 (3): 207-12, 2013.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=23335406&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=23335406&amp;dopt=Abstract">

1618[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

1619</li>

1632

1633

1634

1635 <section id="_45">

1636

1637 <h2>

1638Stage Information for Plasma Cell Neoplasms</h2>

1639

1640 <div id="_section_45" class="pdq-sections">

1641<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1642<h6>

1643In This Section</h6>

1644<ul>

1645<li>

1646<a href="#_234_toc">

1647Multiple Myeloma<ul>

1648<li>

1649<a href="#_49_toc">

1650International staging system</a>

1651</li>

1652<li>

1653<a href="#_53_toc">

1654Genetic factors and risk groups

1655</a>

1656</li>

1657</ul>

1658</a>

1659</li>

1660</ul>

1661</nav>

1662<p id="_46" tabindex="-1">

1663No generally accepted staging system exists for monoclonal gammopathy of undetermined significance, isolated plasmacytoma of bone, or extramedullary plasmacytoma. Of the plasma cell neoplasms, a staging system exists only for multiple myeloma.</p>

1664<section id="_234">

1665<h3 id="_234_toc">

1666Multiple Myeloma</h3>

1667<p id="_47" tabindex="-1">

1668Multiple myeloma is staged by estimating the myeloma tumor cell mass on the basis of the amount of monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein) in the serum and/or urine, along with various clinical parameters, such as hemoglobin and serum calcium concentrations, the number of lytic bone lesions, and the presence or absence of renal failure. Impaired renal function worsens prognosis regardless of stage.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

16691</a>

1670]</p>

1671<p id="_48" tabindex="-1">

1672The stage of the disease at presentation is a strong determinant of survival, but it has little influence on the choice of therapy because almost all patients, except for rare patients with solitary bone tumors or extramedullary plasmacytomas, have generalized disease.</p>

1673<section id="_49">

1674<h4 id="_49_toc">

1675International staging system</h4>

1676<p id="_50" tabindex="-1">

1677The International Myeloma Working Group (IMWG) studied 11,171 patients, of whom 2,901 received high-dose therapy and 8,270 received only standard-dose therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_2.2">

16782</a>

1679] The IMWG evaluated 4,445 patients to create a Revised International Staging System (R-ISS) incorporating lactate dehydrogenase levels and interphase fluorescence <em>

1680in situ</em>

1681 hybridization (I-FISH) results.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

16823</a>

1683]</p>

1684<p id="_51" tabindex="-1">

1685An International Staging System (ISS) was derived and is shown below in Table <a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_52">

16862</a>

1687.[<a href="#cit/section_2.2">

16882</a>

1689]</p>

1744<section id="_53">

1745<h4 id="_53_toc">

1746Genetic factors and risk groups

1747</h4>

1748<p id="_55" tabindex="-1">

1749Newer clinical investigations are stratifying patients with multiple myeloma into so-called good-risk, intermediate-risk, and high-risk groups, based on genetic aberrations detected by I-FISH.[<a href="#cit/section_2.4">

17504</a>

1751-<a href="#cit/section_2.6">

17526</a>

1753] (See Table <a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_442">

17543</a>

1755 below.) This stratification, based on cytogenetic findings, has been derived from retrospective analyses and requires prospective validation.[<a href="#cit/section_2.4">

17564</a>

1757] Bone marrow samples are sent for cytogenetic and FISH analysis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.6">

17586</a>

1759] Plasma cell leukemia has a particularly poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.7">

17607</a>

1761] The otherwise favorable prognosis of hyperploidy is trumped by coexistent adverse cytogenetics.[<a href="#cit/section_2.8">

17628</a>

1763]</p>

1869

1870 <section id="_57">

1871

1872 <h2>

1873Treatment Option Overview for Plasma Cell Neoplasms</h2>

1874

1875 <div id="_section_57" class="pdq-sections">

1876<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1877<h6>

1878In This Section</h6>

1879<ul>

1880<li>

1881<a href="#_59_toc">

1882Asymptomatic Plasma Cell Neoplasms (Smoldering Multiple Myeloma) </a>

1883</li>

1884<li>

1885<a href="#_61_toc">

1886Symptomatic Plasma Cell Neoplasms </a>

1887</li>

1888</ul>

1889</nav>

1890<p id="_58" tabindex="-1">

1891The major challenge in treating plasma cell neoplasms is separating the stable asymptomatic group of patients who do not require immediate treatment from patients with progressive symptomatic myeloma who may need to be treated immediately.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

18921</a>

1893-<a href="#cit/section_3.3">

18943</a>

1895] Monoclonal gammopathy of undetermined significance or smoldering myeloma must

1896be distinguished from progressive myeloma.</p>

1897<section id="_59">

1898<h3 id="_59_toc">

1899Asymptomatic Plasma Cell Neoplasms (Smoldering Multiple Myeloma) </h3>

1900<p id="_60" tabindex="-1">

1901Asymptomatic patients with multiple myeloma who have no lytic bone lesions and normal renal function may be initially observed safely outside the context of a clinical trial.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

19021</a>

1903,<a href="#cit/section_3.4">

19044</a>

1905,<a href="#cit/section_3.5">

19065</a>

1907] Increasing anemia is the most reliable indicator of progression.[<a href="#cit/section_3.5">

19085</a>

1909] The following criteria represent the new definition for smoldering myeloma:[<a href="#cit/section_3.3">

19103</a>

1911]</p>

1912<div class="pdq-content-list">

1913<ul id="_455">

1914<li>

1915Serum monoclonal protein immunoglobulin (Ig) G or IgA of at least 30 g/L or urinary monoclonal protein of at least 500 mg per 24 hours.</li>

1916<li>

1917Clonal bone marrow plasma cells 10% to 60% (&gt;60% represents overt myeloma).</li>

1918<li>

1919Absence of amyloidosis or myeloma-defining events as follows:<div class="pdq-content-list">

1920<ul id="_456" class="list-dash">

1921<li>

1922Hypercalcemia greater than 1 mg/dL higher than normal.</li>

1923<li>

1924Creatinine greater than 2 mg/dL or creatinine clearance less than 40 mL/min. </li>

1925<li>

1926Anemia with hemoglobin less than 10.0 g/dL. </li>

1927<li>

1928Bone lesions (one or more) on skeletal radiography, computed tomography (CT) or positron emission tomography (PET)-CT.</li>

1929<li>

1930Clonal plasma cell percentage in marrow at 60% or more.</li>

1931<li>

1932Involved:uninvolved serum-free light chain (FLC) ratio at 100 or more.</li>

1933<li>

1934More than one focal lesion of at least 5 mm on magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) of the spine.</li>

1935</ul>

1936</div>

1937</li>

1938</ul>

1939</div>

1940<p id="_623" tabindex="-1">

1941A prospective randomized clinical trial investigated the role of immediate therapy for patients with smoldering multiple myeloma by specifying high-risk patients with both 10% or more marrow plasma cells and a serum monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein) of at least 3 g/dL.[<a href="#cit/section_3.6">

19426</a>

1943] The trial randomly assigned 125 patients to receive lenalidomide plus dexamethasone or observation. </p>

1944<div class="pdq-content-list">

1945<ul id="_624">

1946<li>

1947With a median follow-up of 75 months, lenalidomide plus dexamethasone provided benefit in time to progression compared with observation, with a median time not reached (95% confidence interval [CI], 47 months to not reached) compared with 23 months (95% CI, 16&#8210;31 months) (hazard ratio, 0.24; 95% CI, 0.14&#8210;0.41).[<a href="#cit/section_3.6">

19486</a>

1949][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1950Level of evidence B1</a>

1951]</li>

1952<li>

1953There was no difference in overall survival (OS) at a median follow-up of 75 months.</li>

1954<li>

1955At the beginning of this trial, some of the patients had what would now be considered overt myeloma, based on the updated criteria listed above. This may influence the interpretation of the study because overt myeloma patients might be responsible for some of the benefits seen with therapy.</li>

1956</ul>

1957</div>

1958</section>

1959<section id="_61">

1960<h3 id="_61_toc">

1961Symptomatic Plasma Cell Neoplasms </h3>

1962<p id="_62" tabindex="-1">

1963Patients with symptomatic advanced disease require treatment.</p>

1964<p id="_63" tabindex="-1">

1965Treatment most often is directed at

1966reducing the tumor cell burden and reversing any complications of disease, such

1967as renal failure, infection, hyperviscosity, or hypercalcemia, with appropriate

1968medical management. The International Myeloma Working Group (IMWG) has published new criteria for identifying patients with active myeloma who require therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_3.3">

19693</a>

1970] These criteria include the following:

1971 </p>

1972<div class="pdq-content-list">

1973<ul id="_457">

1974<li>

1975Amyloidosis.</li>

1976<li>

1977Hypercalcemia greater than 1 mg/dL higher than normal.</li>

1978<li>

1979Creatinine greater than 2 mg/dL or creatinine clearance less than 40 mL/min. Myeloma can cause renal dysfunction via hypercalcemia, amyloidosis, or light chain deposition disease.[<a href="#cit/section_3.7">

19807</a>

1981]</li>

1982<li>

1983Anemia with hemoglobin less than 10.0 g/dL. </li>

1984<li>

1985Bone lesions (one or more) on skeletal radiography, whole-body MRI or spine and pelvis MRI, or PET-CT scans.[<a href="#cit/section_3.8">

19868</a>

1987]</li>

1988<li>

1989Clonal plasma cell percentage in marrow at 60% or more.</li>

1990<li>

1991Involved: uninvolved serum FLC ratio at 100 or more.</li>

1992<li>

1993More than one focal lesion of at least 5 mm on skeletal bone survey, or if negative, total-body MRI, or MRI of the spine and pelvis, or PET-CT scan.</li>

1994</ul>

1995</div>

1996<p id="_64" tabindex="-1">

1997Response criteria have been developed for patients on clinical trials by the IMWG.[<a href="#cit/section_3.9">

19989</a>

1999] A very good partial response (VGPR) is defined as a reduction of 90% or more in the serum monoclonal protein and a 24-hour urine monoclonal protein of less than 100 mg. Although not incorporated in the IMWG criteria, many trials report near complete response when patients have less than 5% bone marrow plasma cells and unmeasurable serum monoclonal proteins but still have positive serum and/or urine immunofixation. Note that these near complete response patients are incorporated into the VGPR group by the IMWG. Patients who achieve a complete response by IMWG criteria (with a negative immunofixation along with the clear marrow and unmeasurable serum monoclonal proteins) are often said to have attained a stringent complete response if they also normalize their free kappa/lambda light&#8211;chain levels and ratio. The clinical utility of these various categories must be validated in clinical trials. </p>

2000<p id="_65" tabindex="-1">

2001Current therapy for patients with symptomatic myeloma can be divided into the following categories:</p>

2002<div class="pdq-content-list">

2003<ul id="_66">

2004<li>

2005Induction therapies.</li>

2006<li>

2007Consolidation therapies, which are less applicable for patients of advanced age.</li>

2008<li>

2009Maintenance therapies.</li>

2010<li>

2011Supportive care, such as bisphosphonates. For more information, see the <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq#_58">

2012Pharmacological Therapies for Pain Control</a>

2013 section in Cancer Pain.</li>

2014</ul>

2015</div>

2016</section>

2089</a>

2097<section id="_68">

2098<h3 id="_68_toc">

2099Treatment Options for Amyloidosis Associated With Plasma Cell Neoplasms </h3>

2100<p id="_514" tabindex="-1">

2101Treatment depends on assessing the extent of systemic damage from the amyloidosis and the underlying plasma cell dyscrasia.[<a href="#cit/section_4.1">

21021</a>

2103,<a href="#cit/section_4.2">

21042</a>

2105] A rising and elevated level of N-terminal pro brain natriuretic peptide may predict impending cardiac failure in the setting of cardiac amyloidosis, and early treatment should be considered for these patients.[<a href="#cit/section_4.3">

21063</a>

2107]</p>

2108<p id="_69" tabindex="-1">

2109Treatment options for amyloidosis associated with plasma cell neoplasms include the following:</p>

2110<div class="pdq-content-list">

2111<ol id="_70">

2112<li>

2113<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_71">

2114Induction therapy</a>

2115.</li>

2116<li>

2117<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_74">

2118Stem cell rescue</a>

2119.</li>

2120<li>

2121<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_1123">

2122Monoclonal antibody targeting of amyloid deposits</a>

2123 (under clinical evaluation).</li>

2124</ol>

2125</div>

2126<section id="_71">

2127<h4 id="_71_toc">

2128Induction therapy</h4>

2129<p id="_73" tabindex="-1">

2130As is true for all plasma cell dyscrasias, responses have been reported for patients treated with all the same regimens active in multiple myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_4.4">

21314</a>

2132-<a href="#cit/section_4.11">

213311</a>

2134] Lower doses of lenalidomide or pomalidomide must be used in the setting of renal dysfunction.[<a href="#cit/section_4.12">

213512</a>

2136] Daratumumab, with or without other active agents, has also resulted in responses for patients with amyloidosis, usually in combination with other agents used for myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

213713</a>

2138-<a href="#cit/section_4.19">

213919</a>

2140] Rapid responses to induction therapy may result in improvement of renal or cardiac function.[<a href="#cit/section_4.20">

214120</a>

2142]</p>

2143<p id="_1119" tabindex="-1">

2144Evidence (chemotherapy):</p>

2145<div class="pdq-content-list">

2146<ol id="_1120">

2147<li>

2148A prospective randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03201965">

2149NCT03201965</a>

2150) included 388 previously untreated patients with immunoglobulin light-chain amyloidosis (excluding symptomatic myeloma). Patients were randomly assigned to receive to bortezomib, cyclophosphamide, and dexamethasone with or without subcutaneous daratumumab.[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

215121</a>

2152]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2153<ul id="_1121">

2154<li>

2155With a median follow-up of 11.4 months, the hematologic complete response rate was 53% for patients in the daratumumab group and 18.1% for patients in the control group (relative risk, 2.9; 95% confidence interval [CI], 2.1&#8211;4.1; <em>

2156P</em>

2157 &lt; .001). A landmark analysis at 6 months was also performed.[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

215821</a>

2159][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2160Level of evidence B3</a>

2161]</li>

2162<li>

2163Survival free from organ deterioration or hematologic progression or death favored the daratumumab arm (hazard ratio, 0.58; 95% CI, 0.36&#8211;0.93; <em>

2164P</em>

2165 = .02).</li>

2166<li>

2167The cardiac and renal responses were doubled for patients in the daratumumab group, but no statistical analysis was provided.</li>

2168</ul>

2169</div>

2170<p id="_1122" tabindex="-1">

2171A daratumumab combination with bortezomib, cyclophosphamide, and dexamethasone is considered a standard regimen for previously untreated patients who are fit enough to receive this regimen.</p>

2172</li>

2173</ol>

2174</div>

2175</section>

2176<section id="_74">

2177<h4 id="_74_toc">

2178Stem cell rescue</h4>

2179<p id="_76" tabindex="-1">

2180A randomized prospective study of 100 patients with immunoglobulin light-chain amyloidosis compared melphalan plus high-dose dexamethasone with high-dose melphalan plus autologous stem cell rescue.[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

218122</a>

2182] After a median follow-up of 3 years, median overall survival (OS) favored the nontransplant arm (56.9 months vs. 22.2 months; <em>

2183P</em>

2184 = .04).[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

218522</a>

2186][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2187Level of evidence A1</a>

2188] The 24% transplant-related mortality in this series and others reflects the difficulties involved with high-dose chemotherapy in older patients with organ dysfunction.[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

218922</a>

2190-<a href="#cit/section_4.27">

219127</a>

2192] Between 2007 and 2012, the International Blood and Marrow Transplant Research Program identified 800 patients with amyloidosis who underwent autologous stem cell transplantation (SCT); the 5-year OS rate was 77% and transplant-related mortality was 5%, suggesting better selection of patients for transplantation.[<a href="#cit/section_4.28">

219328</a>

2194][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2195Level of evidence C1</a>

2196] Similarly, in a retrospective review of 672 consecutive patients with amyloidosis who underwent autologous SCT over 20 years, the treatment-related mortality declined to 2.4% between 2010 and 2016 in comparison with 8.6% between 2003 and 2009, and 14.5% between 1996 and 2002.[<a href="#cit/section_4.29">

219729</a>

2198][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2199Level of evidence C2</a>

2200] A randomized trial confirming the benefit of autologous transplantation is not anticipated.[<a href="#cit/section_4.3">

22013</a>

2202,<a href="#cit/section_4.30">

220330</a>

2204]</p>

2205<p id="_77" tabindex="-1">

2206An anecdotal series describes full-intensity and reduced-intensity allogeneic SCT.[<a href="#cit/section_4.31">

220731</a>

2208]</p>

2209</section>

2210<section id="_1123">

2211<h4 id="_1123_toc">

2212Monoclonal antibody targeting of amyloid deposits</h4>

2213<p id="_1124" tabindex="-1">

2214The monoclonal antibody CAEL-101 binds to immunoglobulin-associated amyloid in an effort to promote phagocytosis and clearance of the amyloid deposits.</p>

2215<div class="pdq-content-list">

2216<ol id="_1150">

2217<li>

2218In a phase I study (NCT02245867), 27 patients with deep hematologic responses to myeloma therapy, but persistent organ involvement, received CAEL-101.[<a href="#cit/section_4.32">

221932</a>

2220]<div class="pdq-content-list">

2221<ul id="_1151">

2222<li>

2223Fifteen of 24 patients (63%) manifested cardiac, renal, hepatic, gastrointestinal, or soft tissue response by serum biomarkers (such as NT-proBNP), renal function, cardiac function, or imaging studies.</li>

2224</ul>

2225</div>

2226<p id="_1152" tabindex="-1">

2227This treatment is not approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration and is under clinical evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_4.32">

222832</a>

2229][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

2230Level of evidence C3</a>

2231]</p>

2232</li>

2233</ol>

2234</div>

2235</section>

2236</section>

2237<section id="_TrialSearch_67_sid_4">

2238<h3 id="_TrialSearch_67_sid_4_toc">

2239Current Clinical Trials</h3>

2240<p id="_TrialSearch_67_22" tabindex="-1">

2241Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

2242advanced clinical trial search</a>

2243 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

2244General information</a>

2245 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

2383 <section id="_78">

2384

2385 <h2>

2386Treatment of Monoclonal Gammopathy of Undetermined Significance (MGUS)</h2>

2387

2388 <div id="_section_78" class="pdq-sections">

2389<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

2390<h6>

2391In This Section</h6>

2392<ul>

2393<li>

2394<a href="#_79_toc">

2395Treatment Options for MGUS<ul>

2396<li>

2397<a href="#_82_toc">

2398Watchful waiting</a>

2399</li>

2400</ul>

2401</a>

2402</li>

2403<li>

2404<a href="#_TrialSearch_78_sid_5_toc">

2405Current Clinical Trials</a>

2406</li>

2407</ul>

2408</nav>

2409<section id="_79">

2410<h3 id="_79_toc">

2411Treatment Options for MGUS</h3>

2412<p id="_80" tabindex="-1">

2413Treatment options for MGUS include the following:</p>

2414<div class="pdq-content-list">

2415<ol id="_81">

2416<li>

2417<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_82">

2418Watchful waiting</a>

2419.</li>

2420</ol>

2421</div>

2422<section id="_82">

2423<h4 id="_82_toc">

2424Watchful waiting</h4>

2425<p id="_83" tabindex="-1">

2426Multiple myeloma, other plasma cell dyscrasia,

2427or lymphoma will develop in 12% of patients by 10 years, 25% of patients by 20 years, and 30%

2428of patients by 25 years. </p>

2429<p id="_84" tabindex="-1">

2430All

2431patients with MGUS are generally kept under observation to detect increases in

2432M protein levels and development of a plasma cell dyscrasia. Higher levels of initial M protein levels may correlate with increased risk of progression to multiple myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

24331</a>

2434,<a href="#cit/section_5.2">

24352</a>

2436] In a large retrospective report, the risk of progression at 20 years was 14% for an initial monoclonal protein level of 0.5 g/dL or less, 25% for a level of 1.5 g/dL, 41% for a level of 2.0 g/dL, 49% for a level of 2.5 g/dL, and 64% for a level of 3.0 g/dL.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

24371</a>

2438]</p>

2439<p id="_85" tabindex="-1">

2440Treatment

2441is delayed until the disease progresses to the stage that symptoms or signs

2442appear.</p>

2443<p id="_86" tabindex="-1">

2444Patients with MGUS or smoldering myeloma do not respond more

2445frequently, achieve longer remissions, or have improved survival if chemotherapy is

2446started early while they are still asymptomatic as opposed to waiting for

2447progression before treatment is initiated.[<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

24483</a>

2449-<a href="#cit/section_5.6">

24506</a>

2451] Newer therapies have not been proven to prevent or delay the progression of MGUS to a plasma cell dyscrasia.[<a href="#cit/section_5.2">

24522</a>

2453]</p>

2454</section>

2455</section>

2456<section id="_TrialSearch_78_sid_5">

2457<h3 id="_TrialSearch_78_sid_5_toc">

2458Current Clinical Trials</h3>

2459<p id="_TrialSearch_78_22" tabindex="-1">

2460Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

2461advanced clinical trial search</a>

2462 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

2463General information</a>

2464 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

2465</section>

2518 <h2>

2519Treatment of Isolated Plasmacytoma of Bone</h2>

2520

2521 <div id="_section_89" class="pdq-sections">

2528Treatment Options for Isolated Plasmacytoma of Bone<ul>

2529<li>

2536</li>

2537</ul>

2538</a>

2546<section id="_90">

2547<h3 id="_90_toc">

2548Treatment Options for Isolated Plasmacytoma of Bone</h3>

2549<p id="_91" tabindex="-1">

2550Treatment options for isolated plasmacytoma of bone include the following:</p>

2551<div class="pdq-content-list">

2552<ol id="_92">

2553<li>

2554<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_93">

2555Radiation therapy</a>

2556 to the lesion.

2557</li>

2558<li>

2559<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_96">

2560Chemotherapy</a>

2561 (if the monoclonal [or myeloma] protein [M protein] increases and other evidence of symptomatic multiple

2562myeloma occurs).</li>

2563</ol>

2564</div>

2565<section id="_93">

2566<h4 id="_93_toc">

2567Radiation therapy</h4>

2568<p id="_94" tabindex="-1">

2569About 25% of patients have a serum and/or urine M protein; generally, this disappears after adequate radiation therapy to the lytic lesion. </p>

2570<p id="_95" tabindex="-1">

2571The survival rate of patients with

2572isolated plasmacytoma of bone treated with radiation therapy to the lesion is greater than 50%

2573at 10 years, which is much better than the survival rate of patients with disseminated multiple

2574myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

25751</a>

2576]</p>

2577</section>

2578<section id="_96">

2579<h4 id="_96_toc">

2580Chemotherapy</h4>

2581<p id="_97" tabindex="-1">

2582Most patients will eventually develop disseminated disease and

2583require chemotherapy; almost 50% of them will do so within 2 years of

2584diagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

25852</a>

2586,<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

25873</a>

2588] However, patients with serum paraprotein or Bence Jones

2589protein, who have complete disappearance of these proteins after radiation

2590therapy, may be expected to remain free of disease for prolonged periods.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

25912</a>

2592,<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

25934</a>

2594] Patients with a negative flow cytometry on bone marrow examination for plasma cell infiltration are also unlikely to relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

25955</a>

2596] Patients who progress to multiple myeloma tend to have good responses to

2597chemotherapy with a median survival of 63 months after progression.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

25982</a>

2599,<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

26004</a>

2601]</p>

2602</section>

2603</section>

2609advanced clinical trial search</a>

2610 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

2611General information</a>

2612 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

2664<section id="_101">

2665<h3 id="_101_toc">

2666Treatment Options for Extramedullary Plasmacytoma</h3>

2667<p id="_102" tabindex="-1">

2668Treatment options for extramedullary plasmacytoma include the following:</p>

2669<div class="pdq-content-list">

2670<ol id="_103">

2671<li>

2672Radiation therapy to the isolated lesion with fields that cover

2673the regional lymph nodes, if possible.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

26741</a>

2675,<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

26762</a>

2677]</li>

2678<li>

2679In some cases, surgical resection may be considered, but it is usually

2680followed by radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

26812</a>

2682]

2683</li>

2684<li>

2685If the monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein) persists or reappears, the patient may need further

2686radiation therapy. In some patients, the plasmacytoma may shrink, but not disappear, and

2687the M protein persists. Close follow-up is generally warranted for these patients. Surgery

2688often is performed if the plasmacytoma is in a site where it can be removed

2689easily (e.g., in the tonsil); the M protein may disappear from the blood or

2690urine.

2691In other cases, persistence or an increasing M protein may herald progression to multiple myeloma.</li>

2692<li>

2693Chemotherapy is required if the disease progresses and causes symptoms.

2694</li>

2695</ol>

2696</div>

2697<p id="_104" tabindex="-1">

2698Patients with isolated plasma cell tumors of soft tissues, most commonly

2699occurring in the tonsils, nasopharynx, or paranasal sinuses, may need to have

2700skeletal x-rays and bone marrow biopsy (both of which are most often negative) and

2701evaluation for M protein in serum and urine.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

27021</a>

2703-<a href="#cit/section_8.4">

27044</a>

2705]</p>

2706<p id="_105" tabindex="-1">

2707About 25% of patients have serum and/or urine M protein; this frequently disappears after adequate radiation. </p>

2708<p id="_106" tabindex="-1">

2709Extramedullary plasmacytoma is a highly curable disease with progression-free survival ranging from 70% to 87% at 10 to 14 years after treatment with radiation therapy (with or without previous resection).[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

27101</a>

2711,<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

27122</a>

2713,<a href="#cit/section_8.5">

27145</a>

2715]</p>

2716</section>

2717<section id="_TrialSearch_100_sid_8">

2718<h3 id="_TrialSearch_100_sid_8_toc">

2719Current Clinical Trials</h3>

2720<p id="_TrialSearch_100_22" tabindex="-1">

2721Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

2722advanced clinical trial search</a>

2723 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

2724General information</a>

2725 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

2726</section>
