2871<section id="_108">

2872<h3 id="_108_toc">

2873Initial Evaluation</h3>

2874<p id="_109" tabindex="-1">

2875The initial approach to the patient is to evaluate the following parameters:</p>

2876<div class="pdq-content-list">

2877<ol id="_110">

2878<li>

2879Detection and quantification of a monoclonal (or myeloma) protein (M protein) in the serum or urine, and possible immunoparesis (suppression of the other uninvolved immunoglobulins).[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

28801</a>

2881]</li>

2882<li>

2883 Detection of more than 10% of plasma cells on a bone marrow examination, along with flow cytometry, cytogenetics, and fluorescence <em>

2884in situ</em>

2885 hybridization testing.</li>

2886<li>

2887Detection of lytic bone lesions or generalized osteoporosis in skeletal

2888x-rays, or whole-body or spinal and pelvic magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) scans, or focal bone lesions on positron emission tomography-computed tomography (CT) scan.[<a href="#cit/section_9.2">

28892</a>

2890,<a href="#cit/section_9.3">

28913</a>

2892]</li>

2893<li>

2894Presence of soft tissue plasmacytomas.</li>

2895<li>

2896Serum albumin and beta-2-microglobulin levels.</li>

2897<li>

2898Detection of free kappa and free lambda serum immunoglobulin light chain, with calculation of the serum-free light chain ratio.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

28991</a>

2900,<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

29014</a>

2902]</li>

2903<li>

2904Presence of hypercalcemia.</li>

2905<li>

2906Detection of renal dysfunction attributable to the plasma cell dyscrasia (induced by gammopathy or amyloidosis).</li>

2907<li>

2908Presence of anemia.</li>

2909<li>

2910Presence of circulating plasma cells.</li>

2911<li>

2912Presence of hyperviscosity. Asymptomatic patients usually respond to myeloma therapy; plasma exchange is indicated with hemorrhagic or central nervous system manifestations.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

29135</a>

2914]</li>

2915</ol>

2916</div>

2917<p id="_111" tabindex="-1">

2918Treatment selection is influenced by

2919the age and general health of the patient, previous therapy, and the presence of

2920complications of the disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.6">

29216</a>

2922]</p>

2923</section>

2924<section id="_460">

2925<h3 id="_460_toc">

2926Therapeutic Overview</h3>

2927<p id="_461" tabindex="-1">

2928Despite the introduction of many new therapeutic agents over the past two decades, there is still no confirmed curative approach. </p>

2929<section id="_664">

2930<h4 id="_664_toc">

2931Indolent myeloma</h4>

2932<p id="_665" tabindex="-1">

2933Newly diagnosed patients with indolent disease, historically referred to as smoldering myeloma, can be followed on a watchful waiting approach.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

29347</a>

2935] These patients are typically asymptomatic and free of lytic bone lesions, renal dysfunction, hypercalcemia, or significant anemia. Serial measurements of paraprotein parameters can help to confirm stable disease over months or years.[<a href="#cit/section_9.8">

29368</a>

2937]</p>

2938</section>

2939<section id="_666">

2940<h4 id="_666_toc">

2941Symptomatic myeloma</h4>

2942<p id="_667" tabindex="-1">

2943Newly diagnosed patients who require therapy fall into two categories: 1) the younger fit patient who is transplant-eligible or 2) the older more unfit patient with comorbidities who is not transplant eligible. Patients younger than 65 years are usually considered younger and fit, while patients older than 75 years are usually not transplant eligible. Comorbidities and performance status are important determinants at all ages, especially between the ages of 65 years and 75 years, to help decide about transplant eligibility. Nomograms exist for geriatric patients to define life expectancy independent of the myeloma diagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_9.9">

29449</a>

2945] Age, organ dysfunction, and risk of cardiovascular and thrombotic complications influence the choice of induction therapies and consideration of consolidation therapies, such as autologous stem cell transplantation (SCT) consolidation. Most patients also receive medication with a bisphosphonate or RANKL inhibitor to prevent skeletal-related complications.[<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

294610</a>

2947,<a href="#cit/section_9.11">

294811</a>

2949] </p>

2950<p id="_817" tabindex="-1">

2951The International Myeloma Working Group has issued guidance for the diagnosis and management of patients with renal impairment.[<a href="#cit/section_9.12">

295212</a>

2953]</p>

2954<section id="_668">

2955<h5 id="_668_toc">

2956Younger fit patients (transplant eligible)</h5>

2957<p id="_669" tabindex="-1">

2958The younger fit patient will receive induction chemotherapy with a four-drug (quadruplet) or three-drug (triplet) approach that includes bortezomib in the absence of a clinical trial. The most commonly used regimens include:</p>

2959<div class="pdq-content-list">

2960<ul id="_670">

2961<li>

2962D-VRd: daratumumab + bortezomib + lenalidomide + dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.13">

296313</a>

2964,<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

296514</a>

2966]</li>

2967<li>

2968VRd: bortezomib + lenalidomide + dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

296915</a>

2970-<a href="#cit/section_9.18">

297118</a>

2972]</li>

2973<li>

2974CyBorD: cyclophosphamide + bortezomib + dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.19">

297519</a>

2976,<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

297720</a>

2978] This regimen is preferred in the presence of significant renal dysfunction (creatinine clearance less than 45 cc/min). If the renal function recovers rapidly, some clinicians switch to VRd.</li>

2979</ul>

2980</div>

2981<p id="_672" tabindex="-1">

2982After 4 to 8 months of therapy, responding patients may undergo autologous SCT consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

298316</a>

2984,<a href="#cit/section_9.21">

298521</a>

2986] The previously mandated autologous SCT consolidation has been questioned because a large, randomized, prospective trial failed to demonstrate an overall survival (OS) benefit.[<a href="#cit/section_9.22">

298722</a>

2988] Maintenance therapy is then implemented until the time of relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_9.23">

298923</a>

2990-<a href="#cit/section_9.25">

299125</a>

2992] At relapse, subsequent therapies are applied sequentially by using previously successful drugs (if the interval of time since previous exposure is &gt;1 year) or newer drugs not previously tried.</p>

2993</section>

2994<section id="_673">

2995<h5 id="_673_toc">

2996Older unfit patients (not transplant eligible)</h5>

2997<p id="_674" tabindex="-1">

2998The older less-fit patient will receive induction chemotherapy with a triplet regimen (as described for the younger fit patient) plus the CD38-directed monoclonal antibody, daratumumab, or with a doublet regimen and daratumumab, which might be better tolerated.[<a href="#cit/section_9.26">

299926</a>

3000] Therapy is continued until maximal response and then maintenance therapy is applied until relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_9.27">

300127</a>

3002] At relapse, subsequent therapies are given sequentially (as described for the younger fit patient). </p>

3003</section>

3004</section>

3005<section id="_675">

3006<h4 id="_675_toc">

3007High risk versus standard risk</h4>

3008<p id="_677" tabindex="-1">

3009Patients with newly diagnosed or relapsing myeloma can be identified as having standard-risk or high-risk disease. This determination is made on the basis of cytogenetics, genetic aberrations detected by fluorescence <em>

3010in situ</em>

3011 hybridization, and possibly the genetic expression profile analyses that are in the process of standardization.[<a href="#cit/section_9.28">

301228</a>

3013] Plasma cell leukemia at presentation, or as a leukemic evolution of refractory myeloma, is a particularly high-risk, poor-prognosis entity.[<a href="#cit/section_9.29">

301429</a>

3015-<a href="#cit/section_9.32">

301632</a>

3017] Higher-risk patients are candidates for clinical trials employing newer agents upfront or for use of newer combination therapies currently used for relapsed disease at the discretion of the clinician.[<a href="#cit/section_9.33">

301833</a>

3019] Beyond induction therapy, high-risk disease can lead to more aggressive strategies, such as tandem transplantation or consideration of allogeneic SCT. More intensive maintenance therapies may also be given for high-risk disease; instead of using lenalidomide alone, lenalidomide plus bortezomib has been chosen based on prior trials using thalidomide.[<a href="#cit/section_9.34">

302034</a>

3021] These more aggressive strategies have been implemented because of poor responsiveness to standard regimens and the worse prognosis of high-risk patients. Ultimately, randomized prospective trials are needed to establish improved outcomes with these newer approaches for high-risk patients.</p>

3022<p id="_678" tabindex="-1">

3023Unresolved questions regarding therapy for multiple myeloma include the following:</p>

3024</section>

3025<div class="pdq-content-list">

3026<ol id="_462">

3027<li>

3028How do we deal with the financial toxicity of all these advances?</li>

3029<li>

3030The assessment of measurable residual disease (MRD) is mandatory for the assessment of efficacy in clinical trials.[<a href="#cit/section_9.35">

303135</a>

3032-<a href="#cit/section_9.38">

303338</a>

3034] Does this testing outside of the trial setting yield meaningful clinical improvement in patient outcomes by informing selection or duration of therapy? Achievement of MRD negativity after induction therapy (with or without consolidation therapy) is associated with improved progression-free survival (PFS) and, possibly, improved OS.[<a href="#cit/section_9.39">

303539</a>

3036-<a href="#cit/section_9.45">

303745</a>

3038] While MRD negativity may be useful for the design of clinical trials, there are no data suggesting that this interim marker improves outcomes by altering subsequent therapy. Similarly, there are no data to suggest that sustained MRD negativity can allow deintensification or discontinuation of maintenance therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.46">

303946</a>

3040,<a href="#cit/section_9.47">

304147</a>

3042]</li>

3043</ol>

3044</div>

3045</section>

3046<section id="_112">

3047<h3 id="_112_toc">

3048Induction Therapy</h3>

3049<p id="_679" tabindex="-1">

3050Myeloma patients who are symptomatic or require therapy because of progression or adverse laboratory findings will require induction therapy. Ideally, induction therapy should reduce tumor burden, provide symptomatic relief, and prevent further end-organ damage.</p>

3051<section id="_680">

3052<h4 id="_680_toc">

3053Younger fit patients (transplant eligible)</h4>

3054<p id="_681" tabindex="-1">

3055Two randomized prospective trials have established three-drug regimens (triplets) for induction therapy in younger fit transplant-eligible patients).</p>

3056<div class="pdq-content-list">

3057<ol id="_682">

3058<li>

3059In a prospective randomized trial of 525 newly diagnosed patients with myeloma, VRd (bortezomib, lenalidomide, and dexamethasone) was compared with Rd (lenalidomide and dexamethasone).[<a href="#cit/section_9.48">

306048</a>

3061] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3062<ul id="_683">

3063<li>

3064With a median follow-up of 55 months, the VRd group had superior PFS (median PFS, 43 months vs. 30 months [hazard ratio (HR), 0.71; 95% confidence interval (CI), 0.56&#8211;0.91; one-sided <em>

3065P</em>

3066 = .0018]) and superior OS (median OS, 75 months vs. 64 months [HR, 0.79; 95% CI, 0.52&#8210;0.97; <em>

3067P</em>

3068 = .025]).[<a href="#cit/section_9.48">

306948</a>

3070][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3071Level of evidence A1</a>

3072] </li>

3073</ul>

3074</div>

3075</li>

3076<li>

3077A prospective randomized trial of 682 patients older than 65 years compared VMP (bortezomib, melphalan, and prednisone) with melphalan and prednisone alone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

307815</a>

3079]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3080<ul id="_684">

3081<li>

3082With a median follow-up of 60 months, the median OS favored the triplet with bortezomib: 56.4 versus 43.1 months (<em>

3083P</em>

3084 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

308515</a>

3086][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3087Level of evidence A1</a>

3088] </li>

3089</ul>

3090</div>

3091</li>

3092</ol>

3093</div>

3094<p id="_685" tabindex="-1">

3095The U.S. Intergroup and French Inter-Groupe Francophone du My&#233;lome (IFM) study chose VRd as the induction therapy for their prospective randomized trial of 700 patients aged 65 years or younger, which investigated autologous SCT consolidation after three cycles of VRd compared with time to relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

309616</a>

3097] In the United States, VRd has become the standard regimen that is compared to newer combinations for induction therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.18">

309818</a>

3099] Because lenalidomide is metabolized erratically in the setting of renal failure, clinicians often choose the CyBorD regimen (cyclophosphamide, bortezomib, and dexamethasone),[<a href="#cit/section_9.19">

310019</a>

3101,<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

310220</a>

3103] but this selection is empiric and not based on randomized trial results.</p>

3104<p id="_1117" tabindex="-1">

3105The phase II <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02874742">

3106GRIFFIN</a>

3107 trial (NCT02874742) has changed the standard of care for younger, fit, transplant-eligible patients in the absence of fully published comparative data. The trial enrolled 207 patients with newly diagnosed transplant-eligible multiple myeloma. Patients were randomly assigned to receive induction therapy with either D-VRd or VRd. Patients then received autologous SCT, two more cycles of the induction regimen, and 2 years of maintenance therapy with DR (daratumumab and lenalidomide) or lenalidomide alone depending on the original randomization. With a median follow-up of 22.1 months at the clinical cutoff, the percentage of patients with a stringent complete response was 62.6% in the D-VRd group and 45.4% in the VRd group (odds ratio [OR], 1.98; 95% CI, 1.12&#8211;3.49; <em>

3108P</em>

3109 = .0177).[<a href="#cit/section_9.13">

311013</a>

3111] The rate of patients achieving a complete response or better was 79.8% in the D-VRd group and 60.8% in the RVd group (OR, 2.53; 95% CI, 1.33&#8211;4.81; <em>

3112P</em>

3113 = .0045).[<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

311414</a>

3115][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3116Level of evidence B3</a>

3117] The MRD negative rate was 62.5% in the D-VRd group and 27.2% in the VRd group (<em>

3118P</em>

3119 &lt; .0001). These preliminary results warrant consideration of this regimen for first-line therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.49">

312049</a>

3121] A Markov model using MRD status to predict PFS suggests improved quality of life and lower cost over 10 years with the use of daratumumab in the first-line setting.[<a href="#cit/section_9.50">

312250</a>

3123]</p>

3124<p id="_686" tabindex="-1">

3125In younger transplant-eligible patients, alkylators such as melphalan are avoided upfront to prevent stem cell toxicity with subsequent risks for cytopenias, secondary malignancies, or poor stem cell harvesting.[<a href="#cit/section_9.51">

312651</a>

3127] Bortezomib is given subcutaneously, which helps to avoid the neuropathies that were much more severe with intravenous administration.[<a href="#cit/section_9.52">

312852</a>

3129-<a href="#cit/section_9.54">

313054</a>

3131] Bortezomib is also preferred in the setting of renal impairment.[<a href="#cit/section_9.55">

313255</a>

3133] Patients on a bortezomib-containing regimen need prophylaxis for herpes zoster (usually with valacyclovir or acyclovir). Lenalidomide is given orally and can cause an increased risk for deep venous thrombosis (DVT) or pulmonary embolism, requiring additional prophylactic medication.[<a href="#cit/section_9.56">

313456</a>

3135,<a href="#cit/section_9.57">

313657</a>

3137] For patients without extra risk factors for DVT, aspirin (81 mg daily) suffices, but stronger anticoagulants should be considered for patients with multiple risk factors in the presence of lenalidomide (or other similar immunomodulating agents such as pomalidomide or thalidomide). Lower doses of lenalidomide must be used in the setting of renal dysfunction.[<a href="#cit/section_9.58">

313858</a>

3139]</p>

3140</section>

3141<section id="_809">

3142<h4 id="_809_toc">

3143Older unfit patients (not transplant eligible)</h4>

3144<p id="_810" tabindex="-1">

3145Triplet therapies such as VRd and CyBorD can be used in patients in whom fitness is adequate and concurrent morbidities are minimal. When triplets are deemed too difficult, doublets with Vd (bortezomib plus dexamethasone) or Rd (lenalidomide plus dexamethasone) can be used, or even a triplet such as VMP as described in the section for younger fit patients.[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

314615</a>

3147,<a href="#cit/section_9.26">

314826</a>

3149] The advent of daratumumab, the CD38-directed monoclonal antibody, has changed the options since this biological therapy has been studied with the aforementioned doublets and triplets in both phase II and phase III trials.</p>

3150<div class="pdq-content-list">

3151<ol id="_811">

3152<li>

3153In a prospective randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02252172">

3154NCT02252172</a>

3155) of 737 patients with newly diagnosed myeloma who were ineligible for transplantation, daratumumab plus lenalidomide and dexamethasone was compared with lenalidomide and dexamethasone alone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.59">

315659</a>

3157]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3158<ul id="_818">

3159<li>

3160With a median follow-up of 56.2 months, the 60-month OS rate was 66.3% (95% CI, 60.8%&#8211;71.3)% for patients who received daratumumab and 53.1% (95% CI, 47.2%&#8211;58.6%) for patients who received lenalidomide and dexamethasone alone (HR, 0.68; 95% CI, 0.53&#8211;0.86; <em>

3161P</em>

3162 = .0013).[<a href="#cit/section_9.59">

316359</a>

3164][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3165Level of evidence A1</a>

3166]</li>

3167<li>

3168With a median follow-up of 56.2 months, the 60-month PFS rate was 52.5% for patients who received daratumumab (95% CI, 46.7%&#8722;58.0%) and 28.7% for patients who received lenalidomide and dexamethasone alone (95% CI, 23.1%&#8722;34.6%) (HR, 0.53; 95% CI, 0.43&#8722;0.66; <em>

3169P</em>

3170 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.59">

317159</a>

3172]</li>

3173<li>

3174Results for the percentage of patients falling below the threshold for MRD (&lt;1 tumor cell per 10<span class="sup">

31755</span>

3176 white cells) favored the daratumumab combination, 24.2% versus 7.3% (<em>

3177P</em>

3178 &lt; .001).</li>

3179<li>

3180The daratumumab combination resulted in significant and sustained reductions of pain scores and improved quality of life in the EuroQOL 5-dimensional descriptive visual system.[<a href="#cit/section_9.60">

318160</a>

3182][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810021&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810021&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3183Level of evidence A3</a>

3184]</li>

3185</ul>

3186</div>

3187</li>

3188<li>

3189In a prospective randomized trial in 706 patients with newly diagnosed myeloma who were ineligible for transplantation, daratumumab plus VMP was compared with VMP alone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.61">

319061</a>

3191]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3192<ul id="_812">

3193<li>

3194With a median follow-up of 40.1 months, the 3-year OS rate favored the daratumumab-combination group at 78% (95% CI, 73.2%&#8722;83.0%) versus 67.9% in the VMP-alone group (95% CI, 62.6%&#8722;72.6%) (HR, 0.60; 95% CI, 0.46&#8722;0.80; <em>

3195P</em>

3196 = .003).[<a href="#cit/section_9.61">

319761</a>

3198][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3199Level of evidence A1</a>

3200]</li>

3201<li>

3202With a median follow-up of 40.1 months, the 3-year PFS rate favored the daratumumab-combination group at 50.7% (95% CI, 45.1%&#8722;55.9%) versus 18.5% in the VMP group (95% CI, 14.4%&#8722;23.1%) (HR, 0.42; 95% CI, 0.34&#8722;0.51; <em>

3203P</em>

3204 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.61">

320561</a>

3206][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3207Level of evidence B1</a>

3208]</li>

3209<li>

3210Patients without MRD favored daratumumab 22.3% (threshold of one tumor cell per 10<span class="sup">

32115</span>

3212 white cells) versus 6.2% in the control group (<em>

3213P</em>

3214 &lt; .001).</li>

3215</ul>

3216</div>

3217<p id="_813" tabindex="-1">

3218Immunologic reaction to the initial dose of daratumumab can be modulated by splitting the first infusion over 2 days or using the subcutaneous version (not U.S. Food and Drug Administration&#8210;approved).</p>

3219</li>

3220<li>

3221In a prospective randomized trial of 955 patients with newly diagnosed multiple myeloma who were ineligible for transplantation, the combination of carfilzomib plus melphalan and prednisone was compared with the combination of bortezomib plus melphalan and prednisone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.62">

322262</a>

3223]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3224<ul id="_819">

3225<li>

3226With a median follow-up of 23 months, there was no difference in median PFS (22.3 vs. 22.1 months; HR, 0.91; 95% CI, 0.75&#8722;1.10; <em>

3227P</em>

3228 = .159) or in median OS (HR, 1.1; 95% CI, 0.82&#8722;1.4).[<a href="#cit/section_9.62">

322962</a>

3230][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3231Level of evidence A1</a>

3232]</li>

3233</ul>

3234</div>

3235</li>

3236<li>

3237In a prospective randomized trial, 1,087 patients with standard-risk or intermediate-risk myeloma who deferred transplantation for induction therapy were randomly assigned to receive carfilzomib plus lenalidomide and dexamethasone or bortezomib plus lenalidomide and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.63">

323863</a>

3239] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3240<ul id="_1062">

3241<li>

3242With a median follow-up of 26 months, there was no difference in median PFS (34.6 vs. 34.4 months; HR, 1.04; 95% CI, 0.83&#8722;1.31; <em>

3243P</em>

3244 = .742) or in median OS (HR, 0.98; 95% CI, 0.71&#8722;1.36; <em>

3245P</em>

3246 = .923).[<a href="#cit/section_9.63">

324763</a>

3248][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3249Level of evidence A1</a>

3250]</li>

3251</ul>

3252</div>

3253</li>

3254<li>

3255Many other phase II and phase III trials, published in preliminary abstract form, show results similar to the trial that combined daratumumab with melphalan and prednisone, and used daratumumab with other triplets and doublets in both previously untreated and previously treated patients.[<a href="#cit/section_9.64">

325664</a>

3257,<a href="#cit/section_9.65">

325865</a>

3259] Further follow-up is required to establish OS benefits. Mature OS data are required to better assess the cost-effectiveness of daratumumab in the first-line setting.[<a href="#cit/section_9.66">

326066</a>

3261]</li>

3262</ol>

3263</div>

3264</section>

3265</section>

3266<section id="_171">

3267<h3 id="_171_toc">

3268Consolidation Chemotherapy</h3>

3269<section id="_172">

3270<h4 id="_172_toc">

3271Autologous bone marrow or peripheral stem cell transplantation</h4>

3272<p id="_173" tabindex="-1">

3273Evidence (autologous bone marrow or peripheral SCT):</p>

3274<p id="_174" tabindex="-1">

3275The failure of conventional therapy to cure myeloma has led

3276investigators to test the effectiveness of much higher doses of drugs such as

3277melphalan. The development of techniques for harvesting hemopoietic stem

3278cells, from marrow aspirates or the peripheral blood of the patient, and

3279infusing these cells to promote hemopoietic recovery made it possible for

3280investigators to test very large doses of chemotherapy.</p>

3281<p id="_175" tabindex="-1">

3282Based on the experience of treating

3283thousands of patients in this way, it is possible to draw a few

3284conclusions, including the following:</p>

3285<div class="pdq-content-list">

3286<ul id="_176">

3287<li>

3288The risk of early death caused by treatment-related toxic effects has been

3289reduced to less than 3% in highly selected populations.[<a href="#cit/section_9.67">

329067</a>

3291]</li>

3292<li>

3293Extensive prior chemotherapy, especially with alkylating agents,

3294compromises marrow hemopoiesis and may make the harvesting of adequate numbers

3295of hemopoietic stem cells impossible.[<a href="#cit/section_9.51">

329651</a>

3297]</li>

3298<li>

3299Younger patients in good health tolerate high-dose therapy better than

3300older patients with a poor performance status.[<a href="#cit/section_9.68">

330168</a>

3302-<a href="#cit/section_9.70">

330370</a>

3304] However, fit patients older than 70 years can receive autologous SCT consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.71">

330571</a>

3306]</li>

3307</ul>

3308</div>

3309</section>

3310<section id="_177">

3311<h4 id="_177_toc">

3312Single autologous bone marrow or peripheral stem cell transplantation</h4>

3313<p id="_178" tabindex="-1">

3314Evidence (single autologous bone marrow or peripheral SCT):</p>

3315<div class="pdq-content-list">

3316<ol id="_652">

3317<li>

3318While some prospective randomized trials showed improved survival for patients who received autologous peripheral stem cell or bone marrow transplantation after induction chemotherapy compared with chemotherapy alone,[<a href="#cit/section_9.25">

331925</a>

3320,<a href="#cit/section_9.72">

332172</a>

3322-<a href="#cit/section_9.74">

332374</a>

3324][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3325Level of evidence A1</a>

3326] other trials have not shown any survival advantage.[<a href="#cit/section_9.75">

332775</a>

3328-<a href="#cit/section_9.80">

332980</a>

3330][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3331Level of evidence A1</a>

3332] </li>

3333<li>

3334In a prospective randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01208662">

3335NCT01208662</a>

3336), 722 patients aged 65 years or younger with newly diagnosed multiple myeloma received either VRd for three cycles followed by autologous SCT consolidation and two more cycles of VRd or VRd alone for eight cycles. Both groups received maintenance lenalidomide given continuously in the absence of disease relapse or unacceptable side effects.[<a href="#cit/section_9.81">

333781</a>

3338] At relapse, patients who received VRd only (without autologous SCT) were re-induced and offered transplantation if they were still responding.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3339<ul id="_1127">

3340<li>

3341With a median follow-up of 76.0 months, the median PFS was shorter for patients in the nontransplant arm (42.0 months) than for patients in the transplant arm (67.5 months) (HR, 1.53; 95% CI, 1.23&#8211;1.91; <em>

3342P</em>

3343 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.81">

334481</a>

3345][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3346Level of evidence B1</a>

3347]</li>

3348<li>

3349The 5-year OS rate was not significantly different: 79.2% for patients in the nontransplant arm versus 80.7% for patients in the transplant arm (HR, 1.10; 95% CI, 0.73&#8211;1.65; <em>

3350P</em>

3351 &gt; 0.99).</li>

3352<li>

3353Rates of grade 3 or 4 hematologic adverse events were significantly higher in the transplant arm (41.9%) than in the nontransplant arm (26.1%) (<em>

3354P</em>

3355 &lt; .001). Acute myeloid leukemia (AML) or myelodysplastic syndromes (MDS) were only reported in the transplant arm (10 cases).</li>

3356<li>

3357Only 28% of patients who received RVd originally received autologous SCT at any time after the end of study treatment.</li>

3358</ul>

3359</div>

3360</li>

3361<li>

3362Three meta-analyses of almost 3,000 patients showed no survival advantage.[<a href="#cit/section_9.22">

336322</a>

3364,<a href="#cit/section_9.82">

336582</a>

3366,<a href="#cit/section_9.83">

336783</a>

3368][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3369Level of evidence A1</a>

3370]</li>

3371</ol>

3372</div>

3373<p id="_181" tabindex="-1">

3374Even the trials suggesting improved survival showed no signs of a slowing in the relapse rate or a plateau to suggest that any of these patients had been cured.[<a href="#cit/section_9.25">

337525</a>

3376,<a href="#cit/section_9.72">

337772</a>

3378-<a href="#cit/section_9.74">

337974</a>

3380,<a href="#cit/section_9.84">

338184</a>

3382] The role of autologous SCT has changed from a mandated standard consolidation for those patients healthy enough to undergo it toward a therapeutic option, like any other, that offers approximately 2 years of increased PFS on average with defined toxicities. Incorporating, eliminating, delaying, or even replacing autologous SCT in the future (perhaps with chimeric antigen receptor T cells or bispecific antibodies) will be the subject of ongoing and upcoming clinical trials.</p>

3383</section>

3384<section id="_182">

3385<h4 id="_182_toc">

3386Tandem autologous bone marrow or peripheral stem cell transplantation followed by autologous or allogeneic transplantation</h4>

3387<p id="_183" tabindex="-1">

3388Another approach to high-dose therapy has been the use of two sequential episodes

3389of high-dose therapy with stem cell support (tandem transplants).[<a href="#cit/section_9.85">

339085</a>

3391-<a href="#cit/section_9.89">

339289</a>

3393]</p>

3394<p id="_184" tabindex="-1">

3395Evidence (tandem autologous bone marrow or peripheral SCT):</p>

3396<div class="pdq-content-list">

3397<ol id="_185">

3398<li>

3399A meta-analysis of six randomized clinical trials enrolling 1,803 patients compared single autologous hematopoietic cell transplantation with tandem autologous hematopoietic cell transplantation.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3400<ul id="_186">

3401<li>

3402There was no difference in OS (HR, 0.94; 95% CI, 0.77&#8211;1.14) or in event-free survival (EFS) (HR, 0.86; 95% CI, 0.70&#8211;1.05).[<a href="#cit/section_9.90">

340390</a>

3404][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3405Level of evidence A2</a>

3406]</li>

3407</ul>

3408</div>

3409</li>

3410<li>

3411A prospective randomized trial of 758 patients who completed induction therapy in less than 12 months compared autologous SCT plus lenalidomide maintenance, tandem autologous SCT, and autologous SCT plus VRd maintenance.[<a href="#cit/section_9.91">

341291</a>

3413]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3414<ul id="_871">

3415<li>

3416There was no difference in 38-month PFS (53.9%&#8722;58.5%) and OS (81.8%&#8722;85.4%) rates among these three randomized groups.[<a href="#cit/section_9.91">

341791</a>

3418][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3419Level of evidence A1</a>

3420]</li>

3421</ul>

3422</div>

3423</li>

3424<li>

3425Five different groups have compared single or tandem autologous transplants with one autologous transplant followed by a reduced-intensity conditioning allograft from a human leukocyte antigen (HLA)-identical sibling; treatment assignment was based on the presence or absence of an HLA-identical sibling. The results have been discordant for survival in these nonrandomized trials.[<a href="#cit/section_9.92">

342692</a>

3427-<a href="#cit/section_9.95">

342895</a>

3429][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3430Level of evidence C1</a>

3431]</li>

3432<li>

3433Six clinical trials compared the outcomes of patients receiving tandem autologous transplant with those of patients receiving a reduced-intensity allogeneic SCT after autologous transplant. Patients were assigned to the latter treatments based on the availability of an HLA-matched donor. Two meta-analyses of these data showed that although the complete remission rate was higher in patients undergoing reduced-intensity allogeneic SCT, OS was comparable because of an increased incidence of nonrelapse mortality with allogeneic transplant.[<a href="#cit/section_9.96">

343496</a>

3435,<a href="#cit/section_9.97">

343697</a>

3437][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3438Level of evidence A1</a>

3439]</li>

3440</ol>

3441</div>

3442<p id="_405" tabindex="-1">

3443A Cochrane review of 14 controlled studies found none of the trials helpful for contemporary treatment decisions regarding single versus tandem transplants.[<a href="#cit/section_9.98">

344498</a>

3445] None of the trials employed bortezomib or lenalidomide, and the sharp decrease in compliance with a second transplant complicated sample-size calculations for sufficient statistical power.</p>

3446</section>

3447<section id="_193">

3448<h4 id="_193_toc">

3449Allogeneic bone marrow or peripheral stem cell transplantation</h4>

3450<p id="_194" tabindex="-1">

3451Evidence (allogeneic bone marrow or peripheral SCT):</p>

3452<p id="_361" tabindex="-1">

3453Many patients are not young enough or healthy enough to

3454undergo these intensive approaches. A definite graft-versus-myeloma effect has

3455been demonstrated, including regression of myeloma relapses after the

3456infusion of donor lymphocytes.[<a href="#cit/section_9.99">

345799</a>

3458]</p>

3459<p id="_196" tabindex="-1">

3460Favorable prognostic features included the following:</p>

3461<div class="pdq-content-list">

3462<ul id="_197">

3463<li>

3464Low tumor burden.</li>

3465<li>

3466Responsive disease before transplant.</li>

3467<li>

3468Application of transplantation after

3469first-line therapy.</li>

3470</ul>

3471</div>

3472<p id="_199" tabindex="-1">

3473Myeloablative allogeneic SCT has significant toxic effects (15%&#8211;40% mortality), but the possibility of a potent and

3474possibly curative graft-versus-myeloma effect in a minority of patients may offset the high transplant-related mortality.[<a href="#cit/section_9.99">

347599</a>

3476-<a href="#cit/section_9.101">

3477101</a>

3478] In one anecdotal series of 60 patients who underwent allogeneic SCT, six of the patients relapsed between 6 and 12 years, suggesting that late relapses still occur with this type of consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.102">

3479102</a>

3480]</p>

3481<p id="_200" tabindex="-1">

3482 The lower transplant-related mortality from nonmyeloablative approaches has been accompanied by a greater risk of relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_9.101">

3483101</a>

3484] Since the introduction of lenalidomide and bortezomib, a trial exploring donor versus no donor comparison of autologous SCT versus autologous SCT and nonmyeloablative allogeneic SCT in 260 untreated patients showed no difference in PFS or OS.[<a href="#cit/section_9.103">

3485103</a>

3486][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3487Level of evidence C1</a>

3488] This result contrasted with two older trials (before introduction of lenalidomide and bortezomib), which suggested improvement of PFS and OS with a sibling donor.[<a href="#cit/section_9.94">

348994</a>

3490,<a href="#cit/section_9.104">

3491104</a>

3492][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3493Level of evidence C1</a>

3494] </p>

3495<p id="_446" tabindex="-1">

3496 Six clinical trials compared the outcomes of patients receiving tandem autologous transplant to those of patients receiving a reduced-intensity autologous SCT after autologous transplant. Patients were assigned to the latter treatments based on the availability of an HLA-matched donor. Two meta-analyses of these data showed that although the complete remission rate was higher in patients undergoing reduced-intensity autologous SCT, OS was comparable because of an increased incidence of nonrelapse mortality with allogeneic transplant.[<a href="#cit/section_9.96">

349796</a>

3498,<a href="#cit/section_9.97">

349997</a>

3500][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3501Level of evidence A1</a>

3502] Anecdotal long-term survivals have been reported for patients with therapy-related MDS, AML, acute lymphoblastic leukemia, or chronic myelomonocytic leukemia treated with allogeneic SCT.[<a href="#cit/section_9.105">

3503105</a>

3504]</p>

3505</section>

3506<section id="_660">

3507<h4 id="_660_toc">

3508Salvage autologous bone marrow or peripheral stem cell transplantation after relapse from first transplantation</h4>

3509<p id="_661" tabindex="-1">

3510After relapsing more than 24 months after autologous SCT, 174 patients received reinduction therapy and were then randomly assigned to receive either high-dose melphalan and salvage autologous SCT or oral weekly cyclophosphamide.[<a href="#cit/section_9.106">

3511106</a>

3512] With a median follow-up of 52 months, the median OS was superior for salvage autologous SCT: 67 months (95% CI, 55&#8211;not estimable) versus 52 months (42&#8211;60) (HR, 0.56; 0.35&#8211;0.90; <em>

3513P</em>

3514 = .017).[<a href="#cit/section_9.106">

3515106</a>

3516,<a href="#cit/section_9.107">

3517107</a>

3518][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3519Level of evidence A1</a>

3520]</p>

3521<p id="_820" tabindex="-1">

3522In a retrospective review of 233 patients with refractory myeloma or relapsed and refractory myeloma who underwent a salvage autologous SCT, 81% of patients achieved a partial response (PR) or better.[<a href="#cit/section_9.108">

3523108</a>

3524][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3525Level of evidence C3</a>

3526]</p>

3527</section>

3528</section>

3529<section id="_201">

3530<h3 id="_201_toc">

3531Maintenance Therapy </h3>

3532<p id="_202" tabindex="-1">

3533Myeloma patients who respond to treatment show a progressive fall in the

3534M protein until a plateau is reached; subsequent treatment with conventional

3535doses does not result in any further improvement. This has led investigators

3536to question how long treatment should be continued. No clinical trial has directly compared a consolidation approach with a maintenance approach to assess which is better in prolonging remission and, ultimately, survival.[<a href="#cit/section_9.109">

3537109</a>

3538] Most clinical trials employ one or both.[<a href="#cit/section_9.110">

3539110</a>

3540,<a href="#cit/section_9.111">

3541111</a>

3542] Maintenance trials with glucocorticosteroids [<a href="#cit/section_9.112">

3543112</a>

3544,<a href="#cit/section_9.113">

3545113</a>

3546] and with interferon [<a href="#cit/section_9.114">

3547114</a>

3548] showed very minor improvements in remission duration and survival but with toxicities that outweighed the benefits. The efficacy and tolerability of thalidomide, lenalidomide, bortezomib, and ixazomib in the induction and relapse settings has made these agents attractive options in maintenance trials.[<a href="#cit/section_9.109">

3549109</a>

3550]</p>

3551<section id="_408">

3552<h4 id="_408_toc">

3553Maintenance therapy (lenalidomide, ixazomib, daratumumab alone or in combination)</h4>

3554<p id="_828" tabindex="-1">

3555Evidence (maintenance therapy [lenalidomide, ixazomib, daratumumab alone or in combination]):</p>

3556<div class="pdq-content-list">

3557<ol id="_829">

3558<li>

3559A prospective randomized trial of 460 patients with newly diagnosed multiple myeloma who had completed induction therapy and autologous SCT compared lenalidomide maintenance with placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_9.115">

3560115</a>

3561]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3562<ul id="_872">

3563<li>

3564With a median follow-up of 91 months, the median OS for the lenalidomide maintenance group was 113.8 months (95% CI, 100.4&#8722;not reached) versus 84.1 months for the placebo group (range, 73.8&#8722;106.0 months; HR, 0.61; 95% CI, 0.46&#8722;0.80; <em>

3565P</em>

3566 = .0004).[<a href="#cit/section_9.115">

3567115</a>

3568][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3569Level of evidence A1</a>

3570]</li>

3571<li>

3572This translated to a 5-year OS rate of 76% (95% CI, 70%&#8722;81%) for the lenalidomide group versus 64% (95% CI, 58%&#8722;70%) for the placebo group.</li>

3573</ul>

3574</div>

3575</li>

3576<li>

3577A prospective randomized trial evaluated lenalidomide maintenance in 1,917 patients newly diagnosed with or without transplantation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.116">

3578116</a>

3579] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3580<ul id="_830">

3581<li>

3582With a median follow-up of 31 months, lenalidomide showed improved median PFS, 39 months (95% CI, 36&#8722;42) versus 20 months (range, 18&#8722;22) (HR, 0.46; 95% CI, 0.41&#8722;0.53; <em>

3583P</em>

3584 &lt; .0001), but lenalidomide failed to significantly improve the 3-year OS rate, 78.6% (95% CI, 75.6%&#8722;81.6%) versus 75.8% (72.4%&#8722;79.2%) (HR, 0.87; 95% CI, 0.73&#8722;1.05; <em>

3585P</em>

3586 = .15).[<a href="#cit/section_9.116">

3587116</a>

3588][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3589Level of evidence B1</a>

3590] </li>

3591</ul>

3592</div>

3593</li>

3594<li>

3595A meta-analysis included 1,208 patients newly diagnosed after autologous SCT.[<a href="#cit/section_9.117">

3596117</a>

3597]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3598<ul id="_831">

3599<li>

3600With a median follow-up of 79.5 months, OS was not reached for the lenalidomide maintenance group versus 86 months for the placebo or observation group (HR, 0.75; 95% CI, 0.63&#8210;0.90; <em>

3601P</em>

3602 = .001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.117">

3603117</a>

3604][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3605Level of evidence A2</a>

3606]</li>

3607</ul>

3608</div>

3609</li>

3610<li>

3611A meta-analysis of 7,730 patients in randomized clinical trials investigated lenalidomide or thalidomide maintenance in patients with newly diagnosed myeloma, with or without transplantation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.118">

3612118</a>

3613]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3614<ul id="_832">

3615<li>

3616The immunomodulatory maintenance therapy significantly improved PFS (HR, 0.62; 95% CI, 0.57&#8722;0.67; <em>

3617P</em>

3618 &lt; .001), but failed to significantly improve OS (HR, 0.93; 95% CI, 0.85&#8722;1.01; <em>

3619P</em>

3620 = .082).[<a href="#cit/section_9.118">

3621118</a>

3622][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3623Level of evidence B1</a>

3624] </li>

3625</ul>

3626</div>

3627</li>

3628<li>

3629A meta-analysis of 5,073 patients in randomized clinical trials investigated maintenance therapy in patients with newly diagnosed myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.119">

3630119</a>

3631]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3632<ul id="_833">

3633<li>

3634Lenalidomide (with or without prednisone) significantly improved PFS (HR, 0.47; 95% CI, 0.39&#8722;0.55), but also failed to significantly improve OS (HR, 0.76; 95% CI, 0.51&#8722;1.16).[<a href="#cit/section_9.119">

3635119</a>

3636][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3637Level of evidence B1</a>

3638]</li>

3639</ul>

3640</div>

3641</li>

3642<li>

3643A randomized, prospective trial of lenalidomide maintenance versus no maintenance after induction with melphalan and prednisone or melphalan, prednisone, and lenalidomide included patients aged 65 years and older who were not eligible for transplantation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.27">

364427</a>

3645]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3646<ul id="_834">

3647<li>

3648The results showed a 66% reduction in the rate of progression (HR, 0.34; <em>

3649P</em>

3650 &lt; .001), which translated to an EFS of 31 months versus 14 months in favor of maintenance lenalidomide.[<a href="#cit/section_9.27">

365127</a>

3652][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3653Level of evidence B1</a>

3654] </li>

3655</ul>

3656</div>

3657</li>

3658<li>

3659A randomized prospective trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02541383">

3660CASSIOPEIA</a>

3661 [NCT02541383]) evaluated daratumumab maintenance versus no maintenance for patients with newly diagnosed myeloma. Patients had already received bortezomib, thalidomide, and dexamethasone with or without daratumumab as induction before autologous SCT.[<a href="#cit/section_9.120">

3662120</a>

3663]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3664<ul id="_1118">

3665<li>

3666With a median follow-up of 35.4 months after maintenance randomization, the median PFS was not reached in the daratumumab arm and was 46.7 months (40.0&#8211;not evaluable) with observation only (HR, 0.53; 95% CI, 0.42&#8211;0.68; <em>

3667P</em>

3668 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.120">

3669120</a>

3670][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3671Level of evidence B1</a>

3672]</li>

3673</ul>

3674</div>

3675</li>

3676<li>

3677A randomized prospective trial evaluated ixazomib maintenance versus no maintenance for patients with newly diagnosed myeloma who were not undergoing autologous SCT after induction therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.121">

3678121</a>

3679]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3680<ul id="_1089">

3681<li>

3682With a median follow-up of 41 months, the median PFS favored ixazomib maintenance at 17.4 months versus 9.4 months (HR, 0.66; 95% CI, 0.54&#8211;0.80; <em>

3683P</em>

3684 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_9.121">

3685121</a>

3686][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3687Level of evidence B1</a>

3688]</li>

3689</ul>

3690</div>

3691</li>

3692</ol>

3693</div>

3694<p id="_835" tabindex="-1">

3695All the trials and meta-analyses of lenalidomide maintenance showed a significant improvement in PFS, while OS was improved in one trial and one meta-analysis, both after autologous SCT. All of these trials showed an increase in myelodysplasia or acute leukemia from 3% to 7% for lenalidomide, consistent with other studies of lenalidomide. This increased risk is mostly seen in patients with previous exposure to alkylating agents. Doses of 5 mg to 15 mg a day have been utilized either continuously or with 1 week off every month. For patients unable to receive lenalidomide maintenance, ixazomib is a reasonable alternative. The combination of daratumumab plus lenalidomide is being evaluated in the GRIFFIN trial.[<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

369614</a>

3697]</p>

3698</section>

3699<section id="_410">

3700<h4 id="_410_toc">

3701Proteasome inhibitor maintenance therapy</h4>

3702<p id="_836" tabindex="-1">

3703Evidence (proteasome inhibitor maintenance therapy):</p>

3704<div class="pdq-content-list">

3705<ol id="_837">

3706<li>

3707In a prospective randomized trial of 656 newly diagnosed patients with at least a PR after standard induction therapy followed by autologous SCT, ixazomib (the oral proteasome inhibitor) was compared with placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_9.122">

3708122</a>

3709]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3710<ul id="_838">

3711<li>

3712With a median follow-up of 31 months, the ixazomib maintenance improved medial PFS, 26.5 months (95% CI, 23.7&#8722;33.8) versus 21.3 months (18.0&#8722;24.7) (HR, 0.72; 95% CI, 0.58&#8722;0.89; <em>

3713P</em>

3714 = .0023).[<a href="#cit/section_9.122">

3715122</a>

3716][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3717Level of evidence B1</a>

3718] There was no increase in second malignancies with the proteasome inhibitor (3% for both groups).</li>

3719</ul>

3720</div>

3721</li>

3722<li>

3723In 511 previously untreated patients not eligible for transplant and aged 65 years or older, a randomized comparison of bortezomib, melphalan, prednisone, thalidomide and subsequent maintenance using bortezomib plus thalidomide versus bortezomib, melphalan, and prednisone (with no maintenance) showed superiority of the arm with thalidomide and bortezomib during induction and maintenance.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3724<ul id="_839">

3725<li>

3726With a median follow-up of 47 months, the 3-year PFS rate was 55% versus 33% (<em>

3727P</em>

3728 &lt; .01), and the 5-year OS rate was 59% versus 46% (<em>

3729P</em>

3730 = .04).[<a href="#cit/section_9.123">

3731123</a>

3732][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3733Level of evidence A1</a>

3734] </li>

3735<li>

3736Because of trial design, it is unclear whether the improved results were caused by the addition of thalidomide during the induction or by the use of maintenance therapy with bortezomib and thalidomide.</li>

3737</ul>

3738</div>

3739</li>

3740</ol>

3741</div>

3742<p id="_687" tabindex="-1">

3743Summary: After autologous SCT, patients are offered lenalidomide maintenance therapy based on the consistent PFS and occasional OS benefits previously described. But short-term and long-term toxicities, and financial toxicities, may prevent implementation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.124">

3744124</a>

3745,<a href="#cit/section_9.125">

3746125</a>

3747] High-risk patients, especially those with del(17p) or t(14;16), may require bortezomib maintenance (with or without lenalidomide), but this approach is not evidence-based and confirmatory clinical trials are required.[<a href="#cit/section_9.126">

3748126</a>

3749,<a href="#cit/section_9.127">

3750127</a>

3751]</p>

3752</section>

3753</section>

3754<section id="_300">

3755<h3 id="_300_toc">

3756Management and Prevention of Myeloma Bone Disease</h3>

3757<p id="_688" tabindex="-1">

3758Myeloma bone disease is a consequence of increased osteoclastic activity and agents that inhibit osteoclasts are an important component of myeloma therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.11">

375911</a>

3760] The bisphosphonates pamidronate and zoledronate are used most often, via intravenous infusion, but the RANKL monoclonal antibody inhibitor denosumab, given subcutaneously, is also effective, especially when renal dysfunction precludes the use of bisphosphonates.[<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

376110</a>

3762,<a href="#cit/section_9.11">

376311</a>

3764]</p>

3765<section id="_689">

3766<h4 id="_689_toc">

3767Zoledronate (bisphosphonate)</h4>

3768<p id="_690" tabindex="-1">

3769Evidence (zoledronate):</p>

3770<div class="pdq-content-list">

3771<ol id="_691">

3772<li>

3773A randomized, prospective trial of 1,970 patients compared intravenous zoledronate with oral clodronate in newly diagnosed patients receiving induction chemotherapy with or without consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_9.128">

3774128</a>

3775] With a median follow-up of 3.7 years, zoledronate improved median OS from 44.5 months to 50.0 months (HR, 0.84; 95% CI, 0.74&#8211;0.96; <em>

3776P</em>

3777 = .0118).[<a href="#cit/section_9.128">

3778128</a>

3779][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3780Level of evidence A1</a>

3781] In this trial, both bisphosphonates were continued until time of relapse. As expected, skeletal-related events were also reduced in the zoledronate group (27% vs. 35%; <em>

3782P</em>

3783 = .004).[<a href="#cit/section_9.129">

3784129</a>

3785,<a href="#cit/section_9.130">

3786130</a>

3787]</li>

3788<li>

3789The improvement of median OS with zoledronate was confirmed in a Cochrane network meta-analysis.[<a href="#cit/section_9.131">

3790131</a>

3791][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3792Level of evidence A2</a>

3793] This meta-analysis also showed that 6 to 15 patients need treatment with bisphosphonates to prevent one skeletal-related event.</li>

3794<li>

3795A clinical trial of zoledronate given once a month compared with zoledronate given every 12 weeks showed noninferiority for the 12-week regimen in 1,822 patients with bone metastases from breast cancer, prostate cancer, or multiple myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.132">

3796132</a>

3797] However, this study included only 278 myeloma patients, and evaluation of this subgroup was insufficiently powered to establish noninferiority for the 12-week regimen. Nonetheless, this trial is used as justification for implementing a 12-week schedule at the start of therapy or as soon as maximal response has been reached.</li>

3798<li>

3799 Bisphosphonates are associated with infrequent long-term complications (in 3%&#8211;5% of patients), including osteonecrosis of the jaw and avascular necrosis of the hip.[<a href="#cit/section_9.133">

3800133</a>

3801,<a href="#cit/section_9.134">

3802134</a>

3803] For more information about osteonecrosis of the jaw, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/mouth-throat/oral-complications-hp-pdq">

3804Oral Complications of Chemotherapy and Head/Neck Radiation</a>

3805. These side effects must be balanced against the potential benefits of bisphosphonates when bone metastases are evident.[<a href="#cit/section_9.135">

3806135</a>

3807] Bisphosphonates are usually given intravenously on a monthly basis for 2 years and then extended at the same schedule or at a reduced schedule (i.e., once every 3&#8211;4 months), if there is evidence of active myeloma bone disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.136">

3808136</a>

3809,<a href="#cit/section_9.137">

3810137</a>

3811] The aforementioned randomized trial,[<a href="#cit/section_9.129">

3812129</a>

3813] which showed OS advantage, continued patients on bisphosphonates monthly until time of relapse.</li>

3814</ol>

3815</div>

3816</section>

3817<section id="_692">

3818<h4 id="_692_toc">

3819Pamidronate (bisphosphonate)</h4>

3820<p id="_693" tabindex="-1">

3821Evidence (pamidronate):</p>

3822<div class="pdq-content-list">

3823<ol id="_694">

3824<li>

3825A randomized, double-blind study of patients with stage III myeloma showed that

3826monthly intravenous pamidronate significantly reduced pathological fractures,

3827bone pain, spinal cord compression, and the need for bone radiation therapy (38% skeletal-related events were reported in the treatment group vs. 51% in the placebo

3828group after 21 months of therapy; <em>

3829P </em>

3830= .015).[<a href="#cit/section_9.138">

3831138</a>

3832][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3833Level of evidence B1</a>

3834] For more information about bisphosphonate therapy, see the <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq#_58">

3835Pharmacological Therapies for Pain Control</a>

3836 section in Cancer Pain.</li>

3837<li>

3838A double-blind, randomized, controlled trial with 504 patients with newly diagnosed multiple myeloma compared 30 mg of pamidronate to 90 mg of pamidronate and found there was no difference in skeletal-related events, but there was less osteonecrosis (2 events vs. 8 events) seen in the low-dose group.[<a href="#cit/section_9.139">

3839139</a>

3840][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3841Level of evidence B3</a>

3842]</li>

3843<li>

3844A randomized comparison of pamidronate versus zoledronic acid in 518 patients with multiple myeloma showed equivalent efficacy in regard to skeletal-related complications (both were given for 2 years).[<a href="#cit/section_9.140">

3845140</a>

3846][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3847Level of evidence B1</a>

3848] </li>

3849</ol>

3850</div>

3851</section>

3852<section id="_695">

3853<h4 id="_695_toc">

3854Denosumab (RANKL inhibitor)</h4>

3855<p id="_696" tabindex="-1">

3856Evidence (denosumab):</p>

3857<div class="pdq-content-list">

3858<ol id="_697">

3859<li>

3860In a prospective randomized double-blind trial, 1,718 patients with newly diagnosed myeloma and at least one documented lytic bone lesion received either zoledronate or denosumab.[<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

386110</a>

3862]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3863<ul id="_698">

3864<li>

3865The study met its primary end point of noninferiority for denosumab compared with zoledronate (HR, 0.98; 95% CI, 0.85&#8210;1.14; <em>

3866P</em>

3867 = .01 for noninferiority).[<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

386810</a>

3869]</li>

3870<li>

3871Denosumab is significantly more expensive than the bisphosphonates, which are available in generic form.</li>

3872</ul>

3873</div>

3874</li>

3875</ol>

3876</div>

3877<p id="_827" tabindex="-1">

3878Unlike bisphosphonates, the reversible mechanism of action for denosumab may result in rebound fractures if it is discontinued, although this theoretical concern for myeloma patients may be mitigated by continuous maintenance therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.141">

3879141</a>

3880]</p>

3881</section>

3882<section id="_304">

3883<h4 id="_304_toc">

3884Radiation therapy for bone lesions</h4>

3885<p id="_305" tabindex="-1">

3886Lytic lesions of the spine generally require radiation if any of the following are true:</p>

3887<div class="pdq-content-list">

3888<ol id="_306">

3889<li>

3890They are associated with an

3891extramedullary (paraspinal) plasmacytoma.</li>

3892<li>

3893A painful destruction of a

3894vertebral body occurred.</li>

3895<li>

3896CT or MRI scans present evidence of spinal

3897cord compression.[<a href="#cit/section_9.142">

3898142</a>

3899]</li>

3900</ol>

3901</div>

3902<p id="_307" tabindex="-1">

3903Back pain caused by osteoporosis and small compression fractures of the

3904vertebrae responds best to chemotherapy.</p>

3905<p id="_308" tabindex="-1">

3906Extensive radiation of the spine or

3907long bones for diffuse osteoporosis may lead to prolonged suppression of

3908hemopoiesis and is rarely indicated.[<a href="#cit/section_9.143">

3909143</a>

3910]</p>

3911<p id="_309" tabindex="-1">

3912Bisphosphonates are useful for

3913slowing or reversing the osteopenia that is common in myeloma patients.[<a href="#cit/section_9.138">

3914138</a>

3915]</p>

4566<section id="_945">

4567<h3 id="_945_toc">

4568Treatment Options for Relapsed or Refractory Multiple Myeloma</h3>

4569<p id="_946" tabindex="-1">

4570Relapses occur for almost all patients after induction therapy, consolidation with autologous stem cell transplantation (SCT), and maintenance therapy. During initial therapy, some patients respond poorly or their disease progresses. The general strategy is to apply new therapies sequentially as required. In younger fit patients, reinduction therapy with response may be consolidated with an autologous SCT or allogeneic SCT in some cases. Sometimes, when relapse occurs 1 year or more after initial therapy, the same drugs can be administered a second time.</p>

4571<p id="_947" tabindex="-1">

4572A

4573subgroup of patients who do not achieve a response to induction chemotherapy have stable disease and enjoy a survival prognosis that

4574is as good as that for responding patients.[<a href="#cit/section_10.1">

45751</a>

4576,<a href="#cit/section_10.2">

45772</a>

4578] When the stable nature of the

4579disease becomes established, these patients can discontinue therapy until the

4580myeloma begins to progress again. Others with primary refractory myeloma and

4581progressive disease require a change in therapy. For more information, see the <a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_107">

4582Treatment of Multiple Myeloma</a>

4583 section.</p>

4584<p id="_948" tabindex="-1">

4585For patients who respond to their initial therapy, the myeloma growth rate, as

4586measured by the monoclonal (or myeloma) protein-doubling time, increases progressively with each

4587subsequent relapse, and remission durations become shorter and shorter. Marrow

4588function becomes increasingly compromised as patients develop pancytopenia and

4589enter a refractory phase; occasionally, the myeloma cells dedifferentiate and

4590extramedullary plasmacytomas develop. The myeloma cells may still be sensitive

4591to chemotherapy, but the regrowth rate during relapse is so rapid that

4592progressive improvement is not observed.</p>

4593<p id="_949" tabindex="-1">

4594Combinations of drugs or single agents may be administered sequentially as required. The goal is to avoid symptoms and adverse consequences of relapsing disease; however, the onset of therapy may be delayed because of slow disease progression and good performance status. </p>

4595<p id="_950" tabindex="-1">

4596Treatment options for relapsed or refractory multiple myeloma include the following:</p>

4597<div class="pdq-content-list">

4598<ol id="_951">

4599<li>

4600<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_955">

4601Monoclonal antibodies</a>

4602.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4603<ul id="_952">

4604<li>

4605<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_956">

4606Daratumumab</a>

4607.</li>

4608<li>

4609<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_964">

4610Elotuzumab</a>

4611.</li>

4612<li>

4613<a href="/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq#_1111">

4614Isatuximab</a>

4615.</li>

4616</ul>

4617</div>

4618</li>

4619<li>
