4689<section id="_955">

4690<h4 id="_955_toc">

4691Monoclonal antibodies</h4>

4692<section id="_956">

4693<h5 id="_956_toc">

4694Daratumumab</h5>

4695<p id="_957" tabindex="-1">

4696Daratumumab is a monoclonal antibody targeting CD38 that can be given on its own but is usually given in combination with other drugs. Although it is given as an infusion, the subcutaneous formulation has equivalent efficacy and fewer adverse events.[<a href="#cit/section_10.3">

46973</a>

4698]</p>

4699<p id="_958" tabindex="-1">

4700Evidence (daratumumab):</p>

4701<div class="pdq-content-list">

4702<ol id="_959">

4703<li>

4704In a prospective, randomized trial, 498 previously treated patients were randomly assigned to receive daratumumab plus bortezomib plus dexamethasone or bortezomib plus dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.4">

47054</a>

4706]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4707<ul id="_960">

4708<li>

4709With a median follow-up of 7.4 months, the median progression-free survival (PFS) was not reached in the daratumumab group and was 7.2 months in the control group (hazard ratio [HR], 0.39; 95% confidence interval [CI] 0.28&#8210;0.53; <em>

4710P</em>

4711 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_10.4">

47124</a>

4713][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4714Level of evidence B1</a>

4715]</li>

4716</ul>

4717</div>

4718</li>

4719<li>

4720In a prospective, randomized trial, 569 previously treated patients were randomly assigned to receive daratumumab plus lenalidomide plus dexamethasone or lenalidomide plus dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.5">

47215</a>

4722,<a href="#cit/section_10.6">

47236</a>

4724]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4725<ul id="_961">

4726<li>

4727With a median follow-up of 44.3 months, the median PFS was 44.5 months in the daratumumab group versus 17.5 months in the control group (HR, 0.44; 95% CI, 0.35&#8210;0.55; <em>

4728P</em>

4729 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_10.5">

47305</a>

4731,<a href="#cit/section_10.6">

47326</a>

4733][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4734Level of evidence B1</a>

4735]</li>

4736</ul>

4737</div>

4738</li>

4739<li>

4740In a prospective randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03158688">

4741NCT03158688</a>

4742), 466 previously treated patients were randomly assigned in a 2:1 ratio to receive daratumumab plus carfilzomib plus dexamethasone versus carfilzomib plus dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.7">

47437</a>

4744]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4745<ul id="_1087">

4746<li>

4747With a median follow-up of 27.8 months, the median PFS was 28.6 months (95% CI, 25.6&#8211;29.5) in the daratumumab group and was 15.2 months (11.1&#8211;19.9) in the control arm (log rank <em>

4748P</em>

4749 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_10.8">

47508</a>

4751][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4752Level of evidence B1</a>

4753]</li>

4754</ul>

4755</div>

4756</li>

4757<li>

4758In a prospective randomized trial, 1,304 previously treated patients received either daratumumab plus pomalidomide and dexamethasone (DPd) or pomalidomide and dexamethasone (Pd) alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.9">

47599</a>

4760]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4761<ul id="_1156">

4762<li>

4763With a median follow-up of 16.9 months, the median PFS was 12.4 months (95% CI, 8.3&#8211;19.3) for patients who received DPd and 6.9 months (95% CI, 5.5&#8211;9.3) for patients who received Pd (HR, 0.63; 95% CI, 0.47&#8211;0.85; <em>

4764P</em>

4765 = .0018).[<a href="#cit/section_10.9">

47669</a>

4767][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4768Level of evidence B1</a>

4769]</li>

4770</ul>

4771</div>

4772</li>

4773<li>

4774Several phase I and phase II trials evaluated daratumumab as a single agent for relapsed or refractory multiple myeloma.[<a href="#cit/section_10.10">

477510</a>

4776-<a href="#cit/section_10.12">

477712</a>

4778]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4779<ul id="_962">

4780<li>

4781With a median follow-up of 12 to 17 months, the overall response rate was 31% and 36%, with minimal response or stable disease in about 40% of patients.[<a href="#cit/section_10.10">

478210</a>

4783-<a href="#cit/section_10.12">

478412</a>

4785][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4786Level of evidence C3</a>

4787] </li>

4788</ul>

4789</div>

4790</li>

4791</ol>

4792</div>

4793<p id="_1088" tabindex="-1">

4794In every prospective randomized trial to date, adding daratumumab to other active myeloma combination therapies showed improved responses and PFS when compared with the combination therapies alone.</p>

4795</section>

4796<section id="_964">

4797<h5 id="_964_toc">

4798Elotuzumab</h5>

4799<p id="_965" tabindex="-1">

4800Elotuzumab is a monoclonal antibody directed at SLAMF7 (signaling lymphocytic activation molecule F7).</p>

4801<p id="_966" tabindex="-1">

4802Evidence (elotuzumab):</p>

4803<div class="pdq-content-list">

4804<ol id="_967">

4805<li>

4806A prospective randomized trial of 117 patients who had relapsed or were refractory to both lenalidomide and a proteasome inhibitor were randomly assigned to receive elotuzumab, pomalidomide, and dexamethasone (EPd) versus Pd.[<a href="#cit/section_10.13">

480713</a>

4808]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4809<ul id="_968">

4810<li>

4811With a median follow-up of 46 months, the 4-year overall survival (OS) was 50% for the elotuzumab combination (ELd) compared with 43% for the control group (Ld) (HR, 0.78; 95% CI, 0.63&#8211;0.96).[<a href="#cit/section_10.14">

481214</a>

4813][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4814Level of evidence A1</a>

4815]</li>

4816</ul>

4817</div>

4818</li>

4819<li>

4820In a prospective randomized trial of 646 patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma, elotuzumab was combined with lenalidomide and dexamethasone and compared with lenalidomide and dexamethasone alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.15">

482115</a>

4822][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4823Level of evidence A1</a>

4824]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4825<ul id="_969">

4826<li>

4827With a median follow-up of 2.8 years, the group receiving elotuzumab had a superior 3-year PFS rate of 26% versus 18% (HR, 0.73; 95% CI, 0.60&#8211;0.89; <em>

4828P</em>

4829 = .0014) and improved 3-year OS rate of 44% versus 39% (<em>

4830P</em>

4831 = .0257).</li>

4832</ul>

4833</div>

4834</li>

4835</ol>

4836</div>

4837</section>

4838<section id="_1111">

4839<h5 id="_1111_toc">

4840Isatuximab</h5>

4841<p id="_1112" tabindex="-1">

4842Isatuximab is a monoclonal antibody directed against CD38.</p>

4843<p id="_1126" tabindex="-1">

4844Evidence (isatuximab):</p>

4845<div class="pdq-content-list">

4846<ol id="_1113">

4847<li>

4848In a prospective randomized trial of 387 patients with relapsed or refractory disease, Pd was given with or without isatuximab.[<a href="#cit/section_10.16">

484916</a>

4850]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4851<ul id="_1158">

4852<li>

4853With a median follow-up of 35.3 months, the median OS was 24.6 months (95% CI, 20.3&#8211;31.3) for patients who received isatuximab plus PD and 17.7 months (95% CI, 14.4&#8211;26.2) for patients who received Pd alone (HR, 0.76; 95% CI, 0.57&#8211;1.01; 2-sided <em>

4854P</em>

4855 = .056).</li>

4856<li>

4857Similarly, the median PFS was 17.5 months (95% CI, 14.9&#8211;19.2) for the isatuximab group and 12.9 months (95% CI, 10.1&#8211;16.6) for the Pd group (HR, 0.76; 95% CI, 0.58&#8211;0.99; <em>

4858P</em>

4859 = .020).[<a href="#cit/section_10.16">

486016</a>

4861][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4862Level of evidence B1</a>

4863]</li>

4864</ul>

4865</div>

4866</li>

4867<li>

4868In a prospective randomized trial of 302 patients with relapsed or refractory disease, the combination of carfilzomib and dexamethasone was given with or without isatuximab.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4869<ul id="_1159">

4870<li>

4871With a median follow-up of 20.7 months, the 2-year PFS rate was 68.9% (95% CI, 60.7%&#8211;75.8%) for patients who received isatuximab group and 45.7% (95% CI, 35.2%&#8211;55.6%) for patients who received carfilzomib and dexamethasone alone (HR, 0.53; 99% CI, 0.32&#8211;0.89; 2-sided <em>

4872P</em>

4873 = .0014).[<a href="#cit/section_10.17">

487417</a>

4875][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4876Level of evidence B1</a>

4877]</li>

4878</ul>

4879</div>

4880</li>

4881</ol>

4882</div>

4883<p id="_1160" tabindex="-1">

4884There are no data comparing isatuximab with daratumumab, both of which target CD38. There are no data proving that isatuximab has efficacy in patients with disease that is resistant to daratumumab.</p>

4885</section>

4886</section>

4887<section id="_970">

4888<h4 id="_970_toc">

4889Proteasome inhibitors</h4>

4890<section id="_1050">

4891<h5 id="_1050_toc">

4892Bortezomib</h5>

4893<p id="_1051" tabindex="-1">

4894Bortezomib is the first-in-class proteasome inhibitor that is given subcutaneously on a weekly basis for 3 of every 4 weeks; the subcutaneous route is preferred to the intravenous (IV) route because it causes significantly less neuropathy and no loss of responsiveness.[<a href="#cit/section_10.18">

489518</a>

4896-<a href="#cit/section_10.20">

489720</a>

4898] Bortezomib is metabolized and cleared by the liver, and it appears to be active and well tolerated in patients with renal impairment.[<a href="#cit/section_10.21">

489921</a>

4900,<a href="#cit/section_10.22">

490122</a>

4902] More than 6 months after completion of bortezomib induction therapy, bortezomib can be given again with a 40% overall response rate, according to a meta-analysis of 23 phase II studies.[<a href="#cit/section_10.23">

490323</a>

4904][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4905Level of evidence C3</a>

4906] </p>

4907<p id="_1052" tabindex="-1">

4908Evidence (bortezomib):</p>

4909<div class="pdq-content-list">

4910<ol id="_1053">

4911<li>

4912A prospective randomized study of 669 patients with relapsed myeloma compared bortezomib given by IV with high-dose oral dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.24">

491324</a>

4914]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4915<ul id="_1054">

4916<li>

4917With a median follow-up of 22 months, the median OS was 29.8 months for bortezomib versus 23.7 months for dexamethasone (HR, 0.77; <em>

4918P</em>

4919 = .027) even though the trial allowed crossover after relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_10.24">

492024</a>

4921][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4922Level of evidence A1</a>

4923]</li>

4924</ul>

4925</div>

4926</li>

4927<li>

4928A prospective, randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00103506">

4929NCT00103506</a>

4930) of 646 previously treated patients compared bortezomib plus pegylated liposomal doxorubicin with bortezomib alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.25">

493125</a>

4932]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4933<ul id="_1055">

4934<li>

4935With a median follow-up of 7.0 months, 1-year OS rates were better in patients who received the combination (82% vs. 75%; <em>

4936P</em>

4937 = .05).[<a href="#cit/section_10.25">

493825</a>

4939][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4940Level of evidence A1</a>

4941]</li>

4942</ul>

4943</div>

4944</li>

4945<li>

4946A prospective, randomized trial of 260 newly diagnosed patients aged 65 years and older compared bortezomib, melphalan, and prednisone (VMP) with bortezomib, thalidomide, and prednisone (VTP).[<a href="#cit/section_10.26">

494726</a>

4948]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4949<ul id="_1056">

4950<li>

4951With a median follow-up of 72 months, the median OS favored the VMP arm, 63 months versus 43 months for the VTP group (HR, 0.67; 95% CI, 0.49&#8211;0.91; <em>

4952P</em>

4953 = .01).[<a href="#cit/section_10.26">

495426</a>

4955][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4956Level of evidence A1</a>

4957]</li>

4958</ul>

4959</div>

4960</li>

4961</ol>

4962</div>

4963</section>

4964<section id="_971">

4965<h5 id="_971_toc">

4966Carfilzomib</h5>

4967<p id="_972" tabindex="-1">

4968Carfilzomib is a second-generation proteasome inhibitor that is given by IV (unlike the subcutaneous route for bortezomib). Most studies have employed twice-weekly administration, but once-weekly administration appears at least equally efficacious and safe.[<a href="#cit/section_10.27">

496927</a>

4970]</p>

4971<p id="_973" tabindex="-1">

4972Evidence (carfilzomib):</p>

4973<div class="pdq-content-list">

4974<ol id="_974">

4975<li>

4976A randomized prospective trial included 578 relapsed or refractory myeloma patients.[<a href="#cit/section_10.27">

497727</a>

4978]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4979<ul id="_975">

4980<li>

4981The median PFS of patients who received carfilzomib once a week was significantly better, 11.2 months (95% CI, 8.6&#8210;13.0 months), than twice a week, 7.6 months (95% CI, 5.8&#8210;9.2 months) (HR, 0.69; 95% CI, 0.54&#8210;0.83; <em>

4982P</em>

4983 = .0029).[<a href="#cit/section_10.27">

498427</a>

4985][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4986Level of evidence B1</a>

4987]</li>

4988</ul>

4989</div>

4990</li>

4991<li>

4992In a prospective randomized trial of 792 patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma, the combination of carfilzomib, lenalidomide, and dexamethasone was compared with lenalidomide plus dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.28">

499328</a>

4994]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4995<ul id="_976">

4996<li>

4997With a median follow-up of 67.1 months, median OS in the carfilzomib arm was 48.3 months (95% CI, 42.4&#8210;52.8) versus 40.4 months (95% CI, 33.6&#8210;44.4) (HR, 0.79; 95% CI, 0.67&#8210;0.95; one-sided <em>

4998P</em>

4999 = .009).[<a href="#cit/section_10.28">

500028</a>

5001][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5002Level of evidence A1</a>

5003]</li>

5004<li>

5005In a preplanned subgroup analysis, patients with high-risk cytogenetics (i.e., t(4;14), t(14;16), del(17p)) also had improved PFS for the triplet (23 months vs. 14 months; HR, 0.70; 95% CI, 0.43&#8722;1.16; one-sided <em>

5006P</em>

5007 = .083) and response rates, but the carfilzomib combination did not abrogate the worse prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_10.29">

500829</a>

5009][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5010Level of evidence B3</a>

5011]</li>

5012</ul>

5013</div>

5014</li>

5015<li>

5016A prospective, randomized study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01568866">

5017NCT01568866</a>

5018) of 929 patients compared carfilzomib and dexamethasone with bortezomib and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.30">

501930</a>

5020]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5021<ul id="_977">

5022<li>

5023With a median follow-up of 37 months, the median OS was 47.6 months (95% CI, 42.5&#8211;not evaluable) for the carfilzomib combination compared with 40.0 months (95% CI, 32.6&#8211;42.3) for the bortezomib combination (HR, 0.79; 95% CI, 0.65&#8211;0.96; <em>

5024P</em>

5025 = .020).[<a href="#cit/section_10.30">

502630</a>

5027][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5028Level of evidence A1</a>

5029]</li>

5030</ul>

5031</div>

5032</li>

5033<li>

5034Cardiovascular adverse events such as heart failure, chest pain, and acute coronary syndrome (grade 3 or higher) occurred in 25% of patients, especially in the first 3 months of therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_10.31">

503531</a>

5036,<a href="#cit/section_10.32">

503732</a>

5038]</li>

5039</ol>

5040</div>

5041</section>

5042<section id="_978">

5043<h5 id="_978_toc">

5044Ixazomib</h5>

5045<p id="_979" tabindex="-1">

5046Ixazomib is a second-generation proteasome inhibitor that is given orally on a weekly basis for 3 of every 4 weeks.</p>

5047<p id="_980" tabindex="-1">

5048Evidence (ixazomib):</p>

5049<div class="pdq-content-list">

5050<ol id="_981">

5051<li>

5052In a prospective, randomized trial involving 722 patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma, ixazomib combined with lenalidomide and dexamethasone was compared with a placebo combined with lenalidomide and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.33">

505333</a>

5054,<a href="#cit/section_10.34">

505534</a>

5056]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5057<ul id="_982">

5058<li>

5059With a median follow-up of 2 years, the median PFS was 20.6 months in the ixazomib group versus 14.7 months for the placebo group (HR, 0.66; 95% CI, 0.47&#8211;0.93; <em>

5060P</em>

5061 = .016).[<a href="#cit/section_10.33">

506233</a>

5063][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5064Level of evidence B1</a>

5065]</li>

5066<li>

5067Improved PFS was also seen for high-risk patients (defined by fluorescence <em>

5068in situ</em>

5069 hybridization and cytogenetics).[<a href="#cit/section_10.34">

507034</a>

5071][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5072Level of evidence B1</a>

5073]</li>

5074<li>

5075No grade 3 or 4 neuropathy was seen in any patient treated with ixazomib.</li>

5076</ul>

5077</div>

5078</li>

5079<li>

5080A prospective randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01850524">

5081NCT01850524</a>

5082) included 705 patients with newly diagnosed, transplant-eligible multiple myeloma. The study compared ixazomib combined with lenalidomide and dexamethasone with a placebo combined with lenalidomide and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.35">

508335</a>

5084]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5085<ul id="_1116">

5086<li>

5087With a median follow-up of 53.3 to 55.8 months for each arm, the median PFS was 35.3 months in the ixazomib group versus 21.8 months in the placebo group (HR, 0.830; 95% CI, 0.676&#8211;1.018; <em>

5088P</em>

5089 = .073).[<a href="#cit/section_10.35">

509035</a>

5091][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5092Level of evidence B3</a>

5093] This difference did not meet statistical significance for PFS.</li>

5094</ul>

5095</div>

5096 </li>

5097</ol>

5099</section>

5100</section>

5101<section id="_990">

5102<h4 id="_990_toc">

5103Immunomodulatory agents</h4>

5104<section id="_991">

5105<h5 id="_991_toc">

5106Pomalidomide</h5>

5107<p id="_992" tabindex="-1">

5108Pomalidomide is a third-generation immunomodulatory agent that shows some myelosuppression and an increased incidence of thromboembolic events, as noted with lenalidomide and thalidomide (requiring thromboprophylaxis with aspirin at least), but very little peripheral neuropathy compared with other agents.</p>

5109<p id="_993" tabindex="-1">

5110Evidence (pomalidomide):</p>

5111<div class="pdq-content-list">

5112<ol id="_994">

5113<li>

5114In a prospective randomized trial of 117 patients who had relapsed or were refractory to both lenalidomide and a proteasome inhibitor, patients were randomly assigned to receive elotuzumab, pomalidomide, and dexamethasone versus Pd alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.13">

511513</a>

5116]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5117<ul id="_995">

5118<li>

5119With a median follow-up of 9.1 months, the median PFS was 10.3 months for the elotuzumab combination compared with 4.7 months for the control group (HR, 0.54; 95% CI, 0.34&#8210;0.86; <em>

5120P</em>

5121 = .008).[<a href="#cit/section_10.13">

512213</a>

5123][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5124Level of evidence B1</a>

5125]</li>

5126</ul>

5127</div>

5128</li>

5129<li>

5130In a prospective randomized trial of 559 patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma and previous treatment with lenalidomide, patients were randomly assigned to receive pomalidomide plus bortezomib and dexamethasone versus bortezomib and dexamethasone alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.36">

513136</a>

5132]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5133<ul id="_996">

5134<li>

5135With a median follow-up of 15.9 months, the median PFS favored the pomalidomide combination, 11.2 months (95% CI, 9.7&#8722;13.7) versus 7.1 months (95% CI, 5.9&#8722;8.9) (HR, 0.61; 95% CI, 0.49&#8722;0.77; <em>

5136P</em>

5137 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_10.36">

513836</a>

5139][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5140Level of evidence B1</a>

5141]</li>

5142</ul>

5143</div>

5144</li>

5145<li>

5146For 302 patients with relapsed or refractory disease, Pd (40 mg weekly) was compared with a higher-dose dexamethasone regimen (40 mg daily for 4 days every 8 days).[<a href="#cit/section_10.37">

514737</a>

5148]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5149<ul id="_997">

5150<li>

5151With a median follow-up of 10.0 months, the PFS was superior for the pomalidomide arm, 4.0 months versus 1.9 months (HR, 0.48; 95% CI, 0.39&#8211;0.60; <em>

5152P</em>

5153 &lt; .0001)[<a href="#cit/section_10.37">

515437</a>

5155][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5156Level of evidence B1</a>

5157]</li>

5158</ul>

5159</div>

5160</li>

5161</ol>

5162</div>

5163</section>

5164<section id="_998">

5165<h5 id="_998_toc">

5166Lenalidomide</h5>

5167<p id="_999" tabindex="-1">

5168Lenalidomide is a second-generation immunomodulatory agent that shows increased incidence of thromboembolic events as noted with pomalidomide and thalidomide (requiring thromboprophylaxis with aspirin at least), increased incidence of myelosuppression (more than pomalidomide), and an increased incidence of neuropathy (less than thalidomide, but more than pomalidomide).[<a href="#cit/section_10.38">

516938</a>

5170-<a href="#cit/section_10.42">

517142</a>

5172]</p>

5173<p id="_1000" tabindex="-1">

5174A meta-analysis of 3,254 patients from seven randomized trials showed that lenalidomide was associated with an increased risk of hematologic second primary malignancies (3.1% in patients who received lenalidomide vs. 1.4% in those who did not; HR, 3.8; 95% CI, 1.15&#8211;12.62; <em>

5175P</em>

5176 = .029).[<a href="#cit/section_10.43">

517743</a>

5178] This risk was confined to the combination of lenalidomide and melphalan (HR, 4.86; 95% CI, 2.79&#8211;8.46; <em>

5179P</em>

5180 = .0001) but was not higher for lenalidomide with either cyclophosphamide or dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.43">

518143</a>

5182] A retrospective review of almost 4,000 patients with relapsed or refractory disease who received lenalidomide in 11 clinical trials suggested an increased incidence of nonmelanoma skin cancers.[<a href="#cit/section_10.44">

518344</a>

5184]</p>

5185<p id="_1001" tabindex="-1">

5186As a result of predominant renal clearance, lenalidomide doses need to be reduced in the setting of impaired renal function (creatinine clearance, 30&#8211;50: 10 mg every day; creatinine clearance, &lt;30: 15 mg every other day; dialysis, 15 mg on day after dialysis).[<a href="#cit/section_10.45">

518745</a>

5188] Uncontrolled trials have added clarithromycin (500 mg twice a day) to lenalidomide and dexamethasone, with reports of increased response rates.[<a href="#cit/section_10.46">

518946</a>

5190] Controlled studies are required to establish the value of this approach.</p>

5191<p id="_1002" tabindex="-1">

5192Evidence (lenalidomide):</p>

5193<div class="pdq-content-list">

5194<ol id="_1003">

5195<li>

5196Two prospective randomized and placebo-controlled studies of 351 and 353 patients with relapsed myeloma compared lenalidomide plus high-dose dexamethasone versus high-dose dexamethasone alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.47">

519747</a>

5198,<a href="#cit/section_10.48">

519948</a>

5200]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5201<ul id="_1004">

5202<li>

5203With a median follow-up of 16 to 26 months, the median OS was 29.6 months or more (not reached in one trial) versus 20.2 months to 20.6 months in the control group (HR, 0.66; 95% CI, 0.45&#8210;0.96; <em>

5204P</em>

5205 = .03 in one study [<a href="#cit/section_10.47">

520647</a>

5207] and <em>

5208P</em>

5209 &lt; .001 in the other study).[<a href="#cit/section_10.48">

521048</a>

5211][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5212Level of evidence A1</a>

5213] </li>

5214</ul>

5215</div>

5216</li>

5217<li>

5218A prospective, randomized study of 1,623 transplant-ineligible, previously untreated myeloma patients compared lenalidomide and dexamethasone given until disease progression with a 72-week induction regimen with melphalan, prednisone, and thalidomide (MPT) for 72 weeks.[<a href="#cit/section_10.39">

521939</a>

5220]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5221<ul id="_1005">

5222<li>

5223With a median follow-up of 46 months, there was improved OS for the lenalidomide group, with 4-year OS rates of 52% versus 38% (HR, 0.72; 95% CI, 0.54&#8211;0.96; <em>

5224P</em>

5225 = .02).[<a href="#cit/section_10.39">

522639</a>

5227][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5228Level of evidence A1</a>

5229]</li>

5230</ul>

5231</div>

5232</li>

5233</ol>

5234</div>

5235</section>

5236<section id="_1006">

5237<h5 id="_1006_toc">

5238Thalidomide</h5>

5239<p id="_1007" tabindex="-1">

5240Thalidomide is a first-generation immunomodulatory agent that is not often used because of its sedative and constipating effects, its significant and potentially debilitating neuropathy, and its thrombogenic effect (thromboprophylaxis is required).[<a href="#cit/section_10.49">

524149</a>

5242,<a href="#cit/section_10.50">

524350</a>

5244] Very little myelosuppression is seen with this agent.</p>

5245<p id="_1008" tabindex="-1">

5246Late in the disease course, when all other options have failed, thalidomide can be employed, sometimes with durable responses.[<a href="#cit/section_10.51">

524751</a>

5248] By utilizing a low dose (50 mg by mouth every day), significant sedation, constipation, and neuropathy may be avoided. Thromboprophylaxis with aspirin, warfarin, or low-molecular-weight heparin is required; the choice of therapy depends on pre-existing risk factors.[<a href="#cit/section_10.42">

524942</a>

5250]</p>

5251<p id="_1009" tabindex="-1">

5252Evidence (thalidomide):</p>

5253<div class="pdq-content-list">

5254<ol id="_1010">

5255<li>

5256A meta-analysis of 1,685 previously untreated patients considered six randomized prospective trials comparing thalidomide, melphalan, and prednisone versus melphalan and prednisone alone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.52">

525752</a>

5258]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5259<ul id="_1011">

5260<li>

5261The addition of thalidomide improved median OS from 32.7 months to 39.3 months (HR, 0.83; 95% CI, 0.73&#8211;0.94; <em>

5262P</em>

5263 = .004).[<a href="#cit/section_10.52">

526452</a>

5265][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5266Level of evidence A1</a>

5267]</li>

5268</ul>

5269</div>

5270</li>

5271</ol>

5272</div>

5273</section>

5274</section>

5275<section id="_1012">

5276<h4 id="_1012_toc">

5277Chemotherapy (cytotoxic agents)</h4>

5278<p id="_1013" tabindex="-1">

5279Regimens:</p>

5280<div class="pdq-content-list">

5281<ul id="_1014">

5282<li>

5283Melphalan and prednisone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.53">

528453</a>

5285,<a href="#cit/section_10.54">

528654</a>

5287]</li>

5288<li>

5289Vincristine + doxorubicin (infusion) + dexamethasone (VAD).[<a href="#cit/section_10.55">

529055</a>

5291,<a href="#cit/section_10.56">

529256</a>

5293]</li>

5294<li>

5295Cyclophosphamide (+ bortezomib + dexamethasone in the CyBorD regimen).[<a href="#cit/section_10.57">

529657</a>

5297,<a href="#cit/section_10.58">

529858</a>

5299]</li>

5300<li>

5301Pegylated liposomal doxorubicin (in a modified VAD regimen) [<a href="#cit/section_10.59">

530259</a>

5303,<a href="#cit/section_10.60">

530460</a>

5305] or combined with bortezomib and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.61">

530661</a>

5307]</li>

5308</ul>

5309</div>

5310<p id="_1015" tabindex="-1">

5311Evidence (chemotherapy):</p>

5312<div class="pdq-content-list">

5313<ol id="_1016">

5314<li>

5315A meta-analysis of randomized prospective trials compared melphalan and prednisone with combinations of other cytotoxic agents. No differences were noted in PFS or OS.[<a href="#cit/section_10.54">

531654</a>

5317][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5318Level of evidence A1</a>

5319]</li>

5320<li>

5321The VAD regimen has shown activity in previously untreated patients and in relapsed patients, with response rates ranging from 60% to 80%.[<a href="#cit/section_10.55">

532255</a>

5323,<a href="#cit/section_10.56">

532456</a>

5325][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5326Level of evidence C3</a>

5327] Because of logistics problems delivering a 96-hour infusion of doxorubicin, substitution with pegylated liposomal doxorubicin provides comparable response rates.[<a href="#cit/section_10.59">

532859</a>

5329,<a href="#cit/section_10.60">

533060</a>

5331]</li>

5332</ol>

5333</div>

5334<p id="_1017" tabindex="-1">

5335Chemotherapy alone has been used to obtain a clinical remission after exhausting most of the new regimens, allowing improvement in performance status that may permit subsequent use of clinical trials investigating alternative therapies.</p>

5336</section>

5337<section id="_1018">

5338<h4 id="_1018_toc">

5339CART cells</h4>

5340<p id="_1019" tabindex="-1">

5341A cellular therapy for refractory and/or multiply relapsed myeloma has been introduced, consisting of autologous T cells transduced with an anti-CD19 chimeric antigen receptor (CART-cell therapy), after myeloablative chemotherapy and autologous SCT. This therapy has shown a 50% to 65% complete remission rate and a median PFS of 18 to 20 months in patients from a highly selected nonrandomized series.[<a href="#cit/section_10.62">

534262</a>

5343-<a href="#cit/section_10.68">

534468</a>

5345][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5346Level of evidence C3</a>

5347] A review of management of moderate to severe immune-related adverse events suggests immediate use of corticosteroids and supportive hospital care.[<a href="#cit/section_10.69">

534869</a>

5349] Other molecular targets and expanded clinical approaches are being investigated.[<a href="#cit/section_10.62">

535062</a>

5351,<a href="#cit/section_10.70">

535270</a>

5353][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5354Level of evidence C3</a>

5355]</p>

5356</section>

5357<section id="_1020">

5358<h4 id="_1020_toc">

5359Selinexor</h4>

5360<p id="_1021" tabindex="-1">

5361Selinexor is a selective inhibitor of nuclear export compounds that blocks exportin 1 (which activates tumor suppressor proteins), inhibits nuclear factor &#954;B, and reduces oncoprotein mRNA translation.</p>

5362<p id="_1022" tabindex="-1">

5363Selinexor (evidence):</p>

5364<div class="pdq-content-list">

5365<ol id="_1023">

5366<li>

5367A randomized prospective trial included 402 patients with relapsed or refractory disease. Patients received either selinexor plus bortezomib and dexamethasone (SVd) or bortezomib and dexamethasone (Vd).[<a href="#cit/section_10.71">

536871</a>

5369]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5370<ul id="_1155">

5371<li>

5372With a median follow-up of 13.2 months (SVd) or 16.5 months (Vd), the median PFS was 13.9 months (95% CI, 11.7&#8211;not evaluable) for patients who received SVd and 9.5 months (95% CI, 8.1&#8211;10.8) for patients who received Vd (HR, 0.70; 95% CI, 0.53&#8211;0.93; <em>

5373P</em>

5374 = .0075).[<a href="#cit/section_10.71">

537571</a>

5376][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5377Level of evidence B1</a>

5378] </li>

5379<li>

5380Patients who received the selinexor combination had more thrombocytopenia (39% vs. 17%) and fatigue (13% vs. 1%).</li>

5381</ul>

5382</div>

5383</li>

5384<li>

5385In a phase IIB multicenter study, 122 patients with multiply resistant myeloma refractory to a proteasome inhibitor, an immunomodulatory agent, and daratumumab received oral selinexor and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.72">

538672</a>

5387] High-risk cytogenetics were present in 53% of patients. Patients had received a median of seven previous regimens.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5388<ul id="_1024">

5389<li>

5390A partial response (PR) rate or better was observed in 26% of patients (95% CI, 19%&#8722;35%), with a median duration of response of 4.4 months. The median PFS was 3.7 months; median OS was 8.6 months.[<a href="#cit/section_10.72">

539172</a>

5392][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5393Level of evidence C3</a>

5394]</li>

5395</ul>

5396</div>

5397</li>

5398<li>

5399In a phase II study of 42 patients with relapsed or refractory disease, patients received SVd.[<a href="#cit/section_10.73">

540073</a>

5401]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5402<ul id="_1025">

5403<li>

5404A partial response or better was observed in 63% of patients, with a median PFS of 9.0 months.[<a href="#cit/section_10.73">

540573</a>

5406][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5407Level of evidence C3</a>

5408]</li>

5409</ul>

5410</div>

5411</li>

5412</ol>

5413</div>

5414<p id="_1085" tabindex="-1">

5415Selinexor has significant side effects, including nausea, vomiting, fatigue, diarrhea, weight loss, poor appetite, and cytopenias. A descriptive retrospective study of 437 patients enrolled in clinical trials focused on aggressive medical support for these side effects.[<a href="#cit/section_10.74">

541674</a>

5417]</p>

5418</section>

5419<section id="_1026">

5420<h4 id="_1026_toc">

5421Venetoclax</h4>

5422<p id="_1027" tabindex="-1">

5423Venetoclax is a selective BCL-2 inhibitor that induces apoptosis in myeloma cells, particularly in those with t(11;14) which expresses high levels of bcl2.</p>

5424<p id="_1028" tabindex="-1">

5425Evidence (venetoclax):</p>

5426<div class="pdq-content-list">

5427<ol id="_1029">

5428<li>

5429In a phase I study of 66 heavily pretreated patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma, 30 patients harbored a t(11;14) translocation.[<a href="#cit/section_10.75">

543075</a>

5431]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5432<ul id="_1030">

5433<li>

5434Among all 66 patients, the overall response rate was 21%, and 15% of patients achieved very good partial response or better. For those with t(11;14), the overall response rate was 40%, with 27% achieving a very good partial response or better.[<a href="#cit/section_10.75">

543575</a>

5436][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5437Level of evidence C3</a>

5438]</li>

5439</ul>

5440</div>

5441</li>

5442<li>

5443In a prospective randomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02755597">

5444BELLINI</a>

5445 [NCT02755597]), 291 patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma were randomly assigned to receive venetoclax plus bortezomib and dexamethasone versus placebo plus bortezomib and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_10.76">

544676</a>

5447]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5448<ul id="_1086">

5449<li>

5450With a median follow-up of 18.7 months, the median PFS was 22.4 months for patients on the venetoclax arm versus 11.5 months for patients on the placebo arm (HR, 0.63; 95% CI, 0.44&#8211;0.90; <em>

5451P</em>

5452 = .01). </li>

5453<li>

5454OS favored the placebo arm because of treatment-related sepsis (HR, 2.03; 95% CI, 1.04&#8211;3.95; <em>

5455P</em>

5456 = .034).[<a href="#cit/section_10.76">

545776</a>

5458][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5459Level of evidence A1</a>

5460]</li>

5461<li>

5462A prespecified analysis of 35 patients with t(11;14) translocation (20 patients who received venetoclax and 15 patients who received placebo) resulted in the median PFS not being reached for patients on the venetoclax arm versus 9.5 months for patients on the placebo arm (HR, 0.11; 95% CI, 0.02&#8211;0.56; <em>

5463P</em>

5464 = .004).[<a href="#cit/section_10.76">

546576</a>

5466][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5467Level of evidence B1</a>

5468]</li>

5469</ul>

5470</div>

5471</li>

5472</ol>

5473</div>

5474</section>

5475<section id="_1063">

5476<h4 id="_1063_toc">

5477BCMA-directed therapy</h4>

5478<p id="_1064" tabindex="-1">

5479The B-cell maturation antigen (BCMA), which is expressed on myeloma cells, has been targeted in CAR T-cell therapy and also using antibody-drug conjugates and bispecific antibody-based molecules.[<a href="#cit/section_10.65">

548065</a>

5481,<a href="#cit/section_10.77">

548277</a>

5483]</p>

5484<p id="_1066" tabindex="-1">

5485Belantamab mafodotin, an anti-BCMA antibody conjugated to the drug mafodotin, resulted in a 32% response rate in 198 heavily pretreated patients.[<a href="#cit/section_10.78">

548678</a>

5487][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5488Level of evidence C3</a>

5489] These results led to U.S. Food and Drug Administration approval for myeloma patients who had received four previous therapies. Severe corneal toxicities in 30% of patients, rarely leading to blindness, mandated ophthalmologic exams before each treatment via a risk evaluation and mitigation strategy program.</p>

5490<p id="_1165" tabindex="-1">

5491Two phase I trials of a bispecific antibody targeting BCMA and T cells included 166 patients who were heavily pretreated. Overall, 68% to 70% of patients responded to the therapy, resulting in a T-cell&#8211;mediated lysis.[<a href="#cit/section_10.79">

549279</a>

5493,<a href="#cit/section_10.80">

549480</a>

5495][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5496Level of evidence C3</a>

5497]</p>

5498</section>

5499<section id="_1035">

5500<h4 id="_1035_toc">

5501Corticosteroids</h4>

5502<p id="_1036" tabindex="-1">

5503Dexamethasone dosage has been evaluated in two prospective randomized trials.</p>

5504<div class="pdq-content-list">

5505<ol id="_1037">

5506<li>

5507A prospective, randomized study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00098475">

5508ECOG-E4A03</a>

5509) of 445 previously untreated patients with myeloma compared lenalidomide and high-dose dexamethasone (40 mg on days 1&#8211;4, 9&#8211;12, and 17&#8211;20, every 28 days) with lenalidomide and low-dose dexamethasone (40 mg on days 1, 8, 15, and 22, every 28 days).[<a href="#cit/section_10.38">

551038</a>

5511]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5512<ul id="_1038">

5513<li>

5514With a median follow-up of 36 months, the 2-year OS rate favored the low-dose dexamethasone arm (87% vs. 75%; <em>

5515P</em>

5516 = .006), despite no difference in PFS.[<a href="#cit/section_10.38">

551738</a>

5518][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5519Level of evidence A1</a>

5520]</li>

5521<li>

5522The increased deaths on the high-dose dexamethasone arm were attributed to cardiopulmonary toxicity. </li>

5523<li>

5524Deep venous thromboses (DVTs) were also more frequent in the high-dose arm (25% vs. 9%). Patients in the low-dose dexamethasone arm with lenalidomide experienced less than 5% DVT with aspirin alone.</li>

5525</ul>

5526</div>

5527</li>

5528<li>

5529A prospective randomized trial of melphalan and prednisone versus melphalan and high-dose dexamethasone showed no difference in PFS or OS, but there was an increase in infection in the high-dose dexamethasone arm.[<a href="#cit/section_10.81">

553081</a>

5531]</li>

5532</ol>

5533</div>

5534<p id="_1039" tabindex="-1">

5535On the basis of these trials, all ongoing trials and regimens use the low-dose dexamethasone schedule in combination with other therapeutic agents: 40 mg dexamethasone (oral or IV) weekly in younger patients or fit older patients, or 20 mg (oral or IV) in less-fit older patients.</p>

5536</section>

5537<section id="_1128">

5538<h4 id="_1128_toc">

5539T-cell-redirecting bispecific antibodies </h4>

5540<p id="_1129" tabindex="-1">

5541T-cell-redirecting bispecific antibodies target both CD3, which is on the surface of T cells, and BCMA (B-cell maturation antigen), which is on the surface of myeloma cells.[<a href="#cit/section_10.82">

554282</a>

5543]</p>

5544<p id="_1130" tabindex="-1">

5545Evidence (teclistamab):</p>

5546<div class="pdq-content-list">

5547<ol id="_1131">

5548<li>

5549Teclistamab, a T-cell-redirecting bispecific antibody, was given to 165 patients with relapsed or refractory myeloma in a phase I/II study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03145181">

5550NCT03145181</a>

5551 and <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT04557098">

5552NCT04557098</a>

5553).[<a href="#cit/section_10.83">

555483</a>

5555]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5556<ul id="_1132">

5557<li>

5558With a median follow-up of 14.1 months, the overall response rate was 63.0%, with a complete response rate of 39.4%. The median duration of PFS was 11.3 months (95% CI, 8.8&#8211;17.1).[<a href="#cit/section_10.83">

555983</a>

5560][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5561Level of evidence C3</a>

5562]</li>

5563<li>

5564Side effects included cytokine release syndrome in 72% of patients (only one patient grade 3 or 4) and hematologic toxicity (grade 3 or 4) in 61% of patients, including febrile neutropenia (44.8%).</li>

5565</ul>

5566</div>

5567</li>

5568</ol>

5569</div>

5570</section>

5571</section>

6063 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

6064

6065 <h2>

6066About This PDQ Summary</h2>

6067

6068 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

6069<section id="_AboutThis_2">

6070<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

6071Purpose of This Summary</h3>

6072<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

6073This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about treatment of plasma cell neoplasms (including multiple myeloma). It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

6074</section>

6075<section id="_AboutThis_4">

6076<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

6077Reviewers and Updates</h3>

6078<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

6079This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

6080PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

6081, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

6082<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

6083 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

6084<div class="pdq-content-list">

6085<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

6086<li>

6087be discussed at a meeting,</li>

6088<li>

6089be cited with text, or</li>

6090<li>

6091replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

6092</ul>

6093</div>

6094<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

6095Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

6096<p id="" tabindex="-1">

6097The lead reviewer for Plasma Cell Neoplasms (Including Multiple Myeloma) Treatment is:</p>

6098<div class="pdq-content-list">

6099<ul id="">

6100<li>

6101Eric J. Seifter, MD (Johns Hopkins University)</li>

6102</ul>

6103</div>

6104<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

6105Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

6106Email Us</a>

6107. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

6108</section>

6109<section id="_AboutThis_10">

6110<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

6111Levels of Evidence</h3>

6112<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

6113Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

6114formal evidence ranking system</a>

6115 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

6116</section>

6117<section id="_AboutThis_12">

6118<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

6119Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

6120<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

6121PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

6122<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

6123The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

6124<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

6125PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Plasma Cell Neoplasms (Including Multiple Myeloma) Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq">

6126https://www.cancer.gov/types/myeloma/hp/myeloma-treatment-pdq</a>

6127. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389362]</p>

6128<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

6129Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

6130Visuals Online</a>

6131, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

6136<h3 id="_AboutThis_17_toc">

6137Disclaimer</h3>

6138<p id="_AboutThis_18" tabindex="-1">

6139Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

6140Managing Cancer Care</a>

6141 page.</p>
